des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the cartilage that is between the two cuts along the bone, then do the other side from the middle incision to the second one, and then pull out this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	insert the instrument called "culter" (which is pointed on one side and soft, not pointed, and its shape is:)
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And cut the bone obliquely towards the skin according to your knowledge, and the bone is soft towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the mid-incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And shave all the hairs that descend from the head towards the incision until the incision is continuous up to the edge of the skin, and then do the other side in the mid-incision; and then equalize the blood and press the wound slightly, and press firmly on the bone for the blood taken; then put a piece of thick cotton in each incision, and put wet bandages soaked in vinegar and oil and asafetida, and ensure that no pus comes out; on the third day remove the sutures, and apply a large amount of fresh mustard paste, then treat with basil oil and other ointments for wound healing until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	the removal of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a person comes with an acute catarrh, you usually see soft and small eyes, and the vision is dimmed, and burned paper particles; hairs fall out, and the head throbs in pain, and the patient coughs; then know by these signs that those substances and this catarrh do not come from anywhere else but from many veins, and the remedy for it, if there is one, is to cure the veins.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you shall tell the patient to bend his head back, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another wide one in the cheek.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 Begin from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; once the bone is exposed, suck all the blood onto a sponge, then put cotton soaked in old linen between the lips of the cut and bind it with bandages soaked in wine and oil, taking care not to cause an abscess to form; once it is removed, you must rub the bone until char starts to grow, then treat it with things that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony and make a plaster with it; administer it to these wounds to encourage char growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear stoppage (stopping/blockage of the ears)
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, beasts, stones or similar things such as iron; seeds, such as peas, beans, and lentils; or flowing substances like water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear stone or another thing that does not fit into the ear, does not lie in the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see a stone, distil a little purple oil or camphor oil and then apply extraction; have the person cough from the shoulders, and stop their nostrils when coughing comes, and place pieces of fabric or wool around the ear; and hold it above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often farting occurs with this treatment; if it does not occur, extract the wind with fine tweezers in this manner:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it farts with tweezers, that's good; if not, bring extraction with a fine thin hook; and if it does not fart with this, make a cane of beeswax and push the head of the cane or the hole of the ear forcefully, and stop the area around the cane with molten wax so that air cannot enter with the cane; then pull it out carefully, as often times it will fart in this way; and if it does not fart in this manner, take glue from where you get it, put it on any instrument that is sharp for this purpose, put some cotton around it; then press the glue against the stone or whatever it may be and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump out of all these things that we have said, then you must hurry to cut the ear before abscess pus comes and spasms; and the method of cutting is that you first anesthetize the patient with the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of its power, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear where the fat or the meat hangs; and let the cut be like a moon, until you reach the bone, then break it as best as you can, and suck quickly with your mouth; and the cure lasts until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is pus that is swelling, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer one thin, subtle sponge according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 make an incision of that grains.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this if you think the grains are moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is even.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In water that falls into the ear, the patient should use warm gargles of first remedies, and fill the ear with large cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on that same ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out because of that, it's good. (This line refers to the cotton in the ear staying in place.)
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If it does not jump out, take many small and light pebbles according to the size of your finger, and heat them slightly in fire; then let the patient take one or more of his fingers and place it into the ear on that side, and press with a stone from the other side on the stone in the ear; and do not stop making stones strike stones until the water completely escapes, and so jumps out entirely; and if you see, take a cord, and push one of the fingers into the ear, and the other end grasp fire as much as the cord gets burned; then change the cords with others until the water completely escapes, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of animals, if it is small like fleas and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large that can be felt, introduce tweezers for extraction; and it is easier to remove whatever is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of parasitic worms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and use distillation methods, and the cure does not help; if you observe no worms, take a piece of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And insert the thin end into the ear according to the amount of pain the patient is experiencing, then press firmly on the entire jawbone; do this repeatedly until all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 If they do not obey and come out, stop the jaw with cotton as I said in the previous section; if they do not swell further as we have mentioned, administer distillations that the ancients have tested for expelling worms, and you will find their methods or instructions for preparing distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this tool, the shape is as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	Let it be made with silver or tin narrowly to a small opening, and above wide for distillation; and for pressing the distillate into one instrument of tin well made for this purpose, take one scraper and wrap around its point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you choose from your medicines into the cane, and let it be in the ear; then push the scraper into the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or turned over in the ear; and the patient should smell the scent inside, and the distillate should be heated with a small flame as if you were distilling it in the ear; but make sure it's not too cold, for the medicine will not be effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear stoppage (stopping/blockage of the ears)
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any ear defects; and this same thing happens in men due to an injury of the ear, or pus born within the ear, and this injury sometimes goes all the way into the ear, if one cannot see it; and sometimes it only affects one side of the ear, and one can clearly see it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if it goes all the way into the ear and cannot be seen, it is grave treatment in many conditions, and in that case you must put the diseased ear in the sun and look inside: if you see the pus appearing, then open it with this spatula as shown here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be careful to make it sharp both in front and behind so that it does not pierce the ear; if the pus is from pus or flesh of the ear, then hold the tweezers subtly and gently remove it until all the pus is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the tumor has invaded fully into the ear, take a sharp, thin scissors and heat it slightly in fire, then insert it into the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the tumor that causes the patient discomfort in the ear, make a small incision carefully, taking care not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a bandage according to the size of the wound and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Keep the dressing moist with rose water and powdered vitriol for each day until the wound is healed. If you see the ear swell up, it is necessary to remove the dressing and replace it with another moistened dressing made of rose oil and beeswax until the swelling goes down; then treat it until it becomes healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, then place it on the ear, and use other treatments to stop the bleeding which are either cauterization or distillation treatments.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of paper (meaning "skin")
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is a remedy for hair that comes from the skin when it is moist and dry; you should stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and strike at their roots with a spatula; then apply powdered vitriol to the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it cannot be plucked out (the hair), then cauterize with the subtle cautery of lentil seeds, and cauterizing after incision is useful; and many times they heal, because nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, the roots burn away and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the hail (meaning "hardened lumps under the skin")
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often in the paper there come certain things that seem to be hard and durable in shape, and because of this it is called "papery tumor," and it is a large assembly of moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is such: watch carefully if the papery tumor becomes soft from both sides, and it is an easy thing to know; then make a wide opening, then scrape off each part gently, then take the tweezers, and squeeze.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it with something and pierce a little bit of paper without causing any harm to the patient, do nothing; if the wound is large, gather it together with stitches and let it heal as long as it heals; if it is small, do not use force because the ointment restores it soon and causes pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the grandine descends inside the ear towards the upper part, invert the paper, grasp the grandine with pliers and crush it and press from both sides; if the paper is pushed back by the incision, do not worry; when the grandine is crushed, apply saltwater oil and care for the area that causes harm until the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 The ointment is spread on the paper cloths above them, and this happens more often with children than with adults, and it causes much pain to their eyes, and they have catarrh in the mornings, and cannot bear the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; therefore, they lie down on their faces immediately, sleep, and keep paper cloths moistened under their eyelids that swell and cover the ointment which opens in oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel something exit between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places their head on a clean surface; then take one linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach from each part, then place it over; press with your hands on either side so that the exinach is enclosed within the circle; then make a slit in the center of the moistener with a sharp lancet, but not larger than the wound made for venesection; and cut the skin completely until you see the exinach; and from various positions comes exinach from the incision, according to the form of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take a piece of coarse cloth between your hands and turn your hand to the left and right until it is spread; and ensure that you do not stray in the incision, that you come entirely to the oil, that you do not pierce it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the beginning of the cut, lift a little on the cut lightly until it opens; then pull out as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and vinegar, and place it on the wound, and hold bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if such men who grind linen and put it on top to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess hot to the joint comes, then heal it with plasters soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	hair from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like growths grow on the eyelids other than nature, and are nourished, they harm the eyes, and cause diseases such as customary tears and swelling of the paper-like growths, until it leads to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways of cure: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine for ague according to what is mentioned in the previous chapter on cautery, or by incision and stitching, or by caustics, as I shall explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper-like growth on the eye towards your left hand; if it is reversed, that is good; if not, poke an awl with one thread over it; and cut off the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow from these hairs, and pull one thread along the entire length of the paper, then shave it; then make a hole in the part below the paper, under the hair-like growths, all the way from the great tear to the small one; then pull out one thread, and place a small tent made of cotton and linen under the paper, then sew a figure similar to the comb of the blackberry bush, and regardless of its shape, it must be according to the quantity that you see needs to lift the paper which is designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if there is a need to apply a large amount of paper, as the paper is softened; then place the entire sponge on top of the two lines you have marked, starting from the large blister and ending at the small one; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the onion into one of the two angles of the keyhole, then peel everything; then bring the two lips together with a stitch of a thin linen thread and squeeze the blood, and remove the excess length of threads on top of the two scissors with anything sticky, if you wish to do so; otherwise, if you don't want to do it, leave the stitch and threads for three or four days; then heal the wound without stitches with drying and binding agents, as the paper revives at the edge of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitch is spoiled (as they say), and this is a laborious work without fear; and if in another way: it is that you sign the paper with a figure similar to the leaves of myrtle, as we have said, at three onions separated according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then fold what is above the small areas equally according to the shape shown below:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the thing is not even, take a needle with thread, and insert it into the figure; insert the other thread through the large incision, and the third thread through the small one, and align the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift the skin as you have said, then sew the two edges of the wound together by stitching, and heal it until it is healed; if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointment and similar soothing ointments; sometimes the hair from the paper is converted: if this occurs, you must use what we have said about the incision; but stitching in one and the other is more artistic.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds is as follows: and it is that you fold the paper and place it inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by hand, and two thin threads equally long as the paper and the thickness of the spatula; take hold of the two corners with these threads; next, bring the two stitched parts together subtly over the top of the folded paper covered by oil, and bind the two stitches from the two sides together; leave it for some days, and the skin that is being bound will die, rot, and fall off, leaving the wound open.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it takes a long time, if it is struck with force, then heal it until it heals; and when the wound is stitched up, and the paper is raised, and the hair will no longer grow; this is the shape of the two canines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operations are such that you take a fine needle, and insert one silk thread of the same fineness; then bring the heads together delicately, and let the length of the threads be about a palm's length; then assemble another fine silk thread briefly, tie the ends of the thread; then put the patient's head in your lap; and expose the operations to the sun so that they are visible, for it is a delicate and small operation, then pierce the needle through the entire chase in the root of the hair adjacent, and make it pass quickly through the skin until you pull it over the natural hair; then remove the hair up to the chase, and insert the removed hair into the chase if there is one or two or three or more; then stretch your hand so that the hairs come out from under the chase with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the chase away to where the thread you ordered has been placed, so that the chase comes out through the hole and can be seen by oil vision; then you will pull the chase and the thread, close the wound and the opening, and leave it for 2 or 3 days, until the hair adheres in its place and new flesh grows; if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from natural growth, and let it grow with that one until it is elongated and then clean it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or pustule comes in the eye, it can come in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly due to a wound or injury, or by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 The method of work in it is that you cut the suture, separate the lips from it, put tents of linen inside and tie it until it heals; you must not use in the treatment of it things that dry out or constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 If you do this, the disease becomes worse than before; but with things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and the juice of watercress or lettuce and flax seed cooked, and immediately afterwards dissolve darnel in any oil, and wrap it in a cloth and apply it to this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you keep it from healing in the same way as it was before; and this work we have said is not without remedy for this disease, so that it does not return in the same way as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the chyle which comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This disease which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauteries and things similar; and the method of work in it is that you take a needle with double thread, and pierce it through the char, so that the threads come out into two cheeks of the char; then place the char above the entire needle, and crush it with a large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shoulder shape returns as it should, that is good; if not, take the rasp and place it in the cleft, turn the shoulder, and make two clefts on its inner side where the shoulder was cut; let the bones of the two clefts be at the two angles of the incision you made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a Greek letter 'I'; then remove that cartilage, according to the thickness where the shoulder meets it, under the skin; then join the two separated parts with a thread of linen; then apply the medicine we mentioned for softening and healing until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, it is necessary to make a flat incision beneath the hairs of the shoulder, as described above; then separate between the two edges of a linen cloth, as I have said; and one should perform the operation according to the shape of the illness, because it is very different in shape, and wise masters prepare engines of all possible power to make the figure return to its natural form. The patient themselves, according to what is necessary for the operation and the application of instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the sudden dislocation of the shoulder
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens in the hands of men in such a way that the paper above is sealed with white oil and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor blade beneath the paper, lift it up; hold it with tweezers, until you grasp what is near the spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too deep so as not to cause pain to the patient because the spatula is too sharp and pierces the oil; and your incision, from which you scrape that assembly, should be light, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and the whole assembly heals, and sometimes there is infection in the sharp oil and leaching of sweet water and colic; then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil and place moist wool on top abundantly of egg; and after the third day use the colic and other healing things until it heals.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two kinds: one is nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles white frozen moisture; when it is touched by iron and boiled in tweezers, it cannot be moved; and both appear starting from the large root and grow little by little until it covers the entire eye and all light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient places his head in your hand, then you pull out the hairs; then take some paper in your hand, then pinch the nail with small tweezers, and extend it; then take a needle, and put on it a horse hair or cow hair or ox hair, and one strong thread; bend the tip of the needle slightly and poke it into the nail, pierce through it entirely, tie the nail with the thread, and extend it above; then scrape off all the skin surrounding the nail root, down to the flesh around it, including the gristle and sinew up to the head of the nail, then chop the remaining part in the root of the nail up to the quick, and scrape off all the subtle tissue and small forces, leaving only the natural flesh or root; and sometimes the nail should be extended only onto the onyx alone, and the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft tissue surrounding it, as described in this form.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the tissue does not touch the flesh and break it, and that the gristle is not pierced; and after the incision pour oil a little amount of broken seed oil, and make a collyrium from litargirium, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with whatever is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerve-ridden and you cannot push the needle in, and the onions cannot enter, it is often cured with medicines for this kind of nail; and they grow as I mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, open the oil of the patient, and take a sharp spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And the nail above shall be finely reamed, and if you see that it does not shrink at all and the reason persists, distill oil of collyrium made from litargyrium and red collyrium and crushed sulphur from your mouth into it; anoint the oil until the next day; then repeat the procedure according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing prevents you in the oil, as in the treatment of an abscess, first milk it, and heal the abscess hot until it is healed, then repeat the procedure as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the sore harms the oil greatly, suspend it at the onion and chop a part of it and not all, so that tears do not come from it; then distill into the oil collyrium red which is made of litargyrium.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Of the flesh which grows upon the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 For some men, a red pustule occasionally grows over the fingernail and covers the skin and turns it towards the palm and resembles a rosebud from balustrade; and the treatment for this is that the patient places their head on the healthy part, then you operate on the nails, and all of that pustule should be cut with appropriate incisions according to its shape, and hold it in place with force; then strike the first part of the pustule, and continue cutting until smooth to the end, making sure not to pierce the oil at the operation; and make an incision similar to the spatula as mentioned in the treatment of the nail and small forces of which one removes the gravel, as shown by this chapter's form; and when the incision is completed and all the pustule is removed, use oil of seil broken or distilled red collyre resembling corrosive medicines, and place cotton with egg white on top to ensure heat over the wound; and if anything remains, or the wound becomes cold, and you doubt about a hot abscess, leave the oil and treat the abscess with calming agents for a hot abscess; then return to your operation until it is healthy, and do the same with all pustules treated in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, you must treat each small wound with natural means; and for an accidental wound, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Should be red veins that are covered on the oil, and they drain their work and weaken the oil day and night.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Therefore, at the beginning you should examine the oil in which the red veins are present and have no other disease except for the sebel; then proceed as follows: instruct the patient to place their head on your healthy side, then press those veins all along for a while according to your wisdom, and let the pressure be subtle double as shown in this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two points in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then make these veins subtle and gentle, and squeeze the blood out one after another, until you see them moving away from the oil; and be careful not to pierce the oil with the tips of the spatula-like instruments, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so as not to burn those veins; and when you have done that, if it distills green and red oil into a colander for correcting what is congealed within the blood.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect everything in that time, make a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and the abscess is certain to heal warmly, then continue as before until it is healthy again; and this is the form of the pressure:
de la fistule de l’oil	From the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The ulcer called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I said earlier, and it is not healed, there is a trap in it that you cut open above the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, you will see the corruption and the blackness; if the joint is all the instrument as in this form; it is called "rough head", and it should be made straight by heating a rod of iron as shown here.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Place the exposed bone in your hand, then turn it between your palms and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption is restored; do this once, then restore the position of healing herbs.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the joint is fused, and char (perhaps cartilage) grows in it, and the body of the bone remains fused for forty days without renewal or becoming abscessed, and no serious accident occurs, knowing that it is healthy; if not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the neck of the bone according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with medicines heated, and when it has been uncovered, take the awl according to this form, and let the point of the awl be at three angles, and the shaft be attenuated up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place it on the bone at the corner of the eye socket, and move your hand away from the oil hole (possibly a small pit or opening), then turn the awl completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the veins if they keep their hand on their neck; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when cartilage grows and hardens the joint, the matter goes to the neck; it is a simpler thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the dislocation
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eyes are fully open and cannot be reduced or diminished in any way, you must tie the patient down; then clean the area with warm water, apply a plaster made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolle, and then secure it using bandages and cloths. The cloths should be soft enough that they can be folded four times and stacked one on top of the other according to the size needed; then secure them with a stiff bandage and renew the plasters without cutting to allow the area to heal. When the plaster has dissolved, remove it and if the eye is healing, it is good; if not, repeat the application of the plaster, cloths, and bandages until the eye heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The double rupture of the ruptured membrane.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the ruptured membrane, and fumigations come out like grains of resin, and it is frightening to see; then if you find it covered, the treatment is such that you thrust an awl into the root of the affected area from beneath up to where it is above, then another awl with a double thread from the edge of the tear; and make it pierce through, and leave the first awl according to its position; then tie the end of the double thread around the eye of the membrane and tighten it well, then withdraw the awl and apply soft oiled linen on top; and let it stay until the threads grow with the membrane, then heal the oil from healing substances as long as the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held in place by the membrane from both sides of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, pierce it with a fine spatula coming from oil, remove the white albugine and drain the eyes, then insert a probe immediately; then withdraw it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bowl of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This illness called "alcunnati" is not far from being assembled in oil, resembling an abscess draining, but it is not an abscess; and the manner of its appearance in the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and upright, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it until you see the abscess rise above your eyes; then it should be lanced, and the abscess and light should not drain, and let the patient observe things as he used to; and if it does not drain below, know that it is an abscess, and if the draining of the abscess is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Make the patient sit between your hands, then take the thin spatulum and place it on the corneal membrane (the conjunctiva with the cornea) I-point, pressing until the bubble forms; and when it is issued, distill into the sharp hot oil mixed with honey, or boiled water and honey, or fenugreek water, then treat it with another cure until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have the appearances of eyes in the division, and what is required for piercing; if it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands in a cross shape (cross-legged), away from sunlight, and hold the oil swab tightly; then put the paper of the oil in your left hand if the eye is on the left side, or in your right hand if the eye is on the right side; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the eye is on the left side, or in your left hand if the eye is on the right side; then put the point of the instrument against the cornea along the thickness of a nail in that white part of the oil at the lower eyelid, then push the almagda instrument skillfully, and hold your hand firmly until it penetrates the white part of the oil, and feel when the almagda reaches the empty space; and the measure of the almagda path should be to the end of the measurement from the pupil to the end of the black line; this is the cornea of the eye, and you will see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument until it reaches the place where the oil is, then press it gently and carefully.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If the wound begins to drain now, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in its oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a little rest, if the wound begins to drain again along the second path, apply force with the instrument, and when it is pushed in and will not go deeper, gently twist your hand around it; then insert another piece of gemstone oil within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then pour in the oil of lavender or moistened cloth soaked in rose oil and abundant egg, and bind it with the oil of lard.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, place a thin layer of beaten egg white on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard hairs, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 Therefore, pierce only the conjunctive, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then push in as much as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare the patient for sleeping in that dimly-lit room where he sleeps on his back; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head either to the right or left, and tie him according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in that same dimly-lit room, test his vision, and have him look at certain things, and then rebind him until the seventh day; and you should not perform this, except during the cure or after the incision now, but you should alleviate it because the wound rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess has come to a head, you should lance the oil before the seventh day, and direct it towards that which soothes abscesses; and when it is appeased, then you should drain the eye (of the abscess) and put silver ointment over its opening for covering any day, and remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then leave the house little by little, and turn to your cases; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country, they make almagda piercings, which causes bleeding, but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, nor have I ever heard of it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of almagda forms, because those who do not know them see them; and they should be of arain properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these should be of the same subtlety, and the rear in four angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh near the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes births or are born diverse kinds of boils, among which some resemble scorpions in shape; and if there are such as have the boil swollen with black color, and if the boil is soft of bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case of the soft cartilage which is not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the onion juice into those cartilages, then pull them out; afterwards hold what you can support with a pointed, sharp spatula on the other side until you know that the cartilage is completely detached.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be held, you should cut it with very thin and light instruments until nothing is left; and if there are abscesses or wounds, use the remedy as appropriate; and if these are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them so that the pus is drained and all the growths are removed, then pour onion juice or vinegar onto the wound.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If it does not open and moisture reaches the palace (the nose), know that it is sound; if moisture does not perforate as it should, know that there is a cartilage grown on the bone above, so the instrument will not come to cut: then you should tie a large piece of linen thread with your hands and leave enough space between each knot; put the patient's chin into the thread loop in his mouth as far as he can, and pull it out while smelling until it comes from his nose; and children at school often do this, and it is easy for whoever wants to perform it; then hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know which one comes after the other by us who are at the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Make sure you know that they have corrupted the flesh there, then draw out the pus, squeeze the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded everything that remains of the flesh; and then put a plaster of wood on it for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, as one distills oils and medicines in the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and lead it thus; and if you see (a tumor), make a closed cane, and let the instrument be filled with oil or any liquid to purify the bladder; and have one handle on the bladder to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	In the head of the nose often arises a disease called 'telul', which grows and becomes large, appearing noticeable to the eye; therefore it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and burn it completely with cautery or hot medicine; and if it is delayed in being cut until it has become large, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as this is an abscess inflamed, for when one cuts it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft touching, not dark colored, you can cover it completely, but be careful that the patient does not feel fear, and treat the area with drying and constricting agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 When solutions come continuously into one of these work cartilages, it helps little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when such a thing happens to anyone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring together the two lips with a stitch, heal it until it is healed; and if the lips have already separated from both sides, you must cauterize all their parts with lime until they heal, then bring together the two lips with a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood and finely ground incense on top; place a piece of plaster of strong or another kind that adheres, on top of the powders, and let it stay until it burns through it, then heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is that you bring together the solution: either with needles, as I have told you in the abdominal stitching; or with thread, as we said before.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips of an abscess
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	For men, within the lips there occurs an abscess hard, resembling grains of peas, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, cut above each tooth, take it with pincers and crush in every part; afterwards apply the leech (leive) juice after the incision of vitriol powder, until the blood is stopped; then apply the lard (aisil) to the wound until it heals.
de la char des gencives	From the jawbone
