Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swelling arises on the jawbone, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and crush its root, letting the blood flow; then apply vitriol powder or other drying powders to the area; if the swelling returns after the incision, as often happens, then you should crush it again and cauterize; it will not return after being cauterized; these are the forms of tools for covering.
des sordens	The sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes sores are assembled at the root of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth turn black and greenish and decay, as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth smell; you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and scrape the sores or the scabs that appear, until there is nothing left; and do the same with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowish and other spots, as long as they are cleaned; and if you remove what is at the first sign, it is good; if not, repeat on the second day and the third, as long as you have finished everything; and know that the teeth require various types of instruments for scraping, according to what the work shows, because the one who scatters the teeth has different shapes than the one who scrapes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary that when you treat the tooth of its pain, you delay pulling it out as long as possible, for this should not be done; for this is a very high substance up to where there is no excuse for shaving.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then, when the patient is compelled to draw (something), it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth pulling.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often the patient feels pain and believes that it is a bad tooth, and tries to draw out the healthy tooth; however, the pain does not stop until the bad one has been removed, as we have seen with such patients; and when you are certain of the tooth pulling, you should first sharpen the instrument around the tooth in all directions; then move it towards your fingers or delicate pliers at the root end bit by bit, until it is loosened, then firmly hold the pliers; and keep the patient's head between your thighs, and hold him tightly so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After straightening the tooth without breaking it, if it does not come out on its own, take any of these instruments and gently push it from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten, it is necessary that you fill it with bandages where the wounds are; and gently tighten it with pliers so as not to break it while tightening; and it must be operated very carefully around the gums to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be careful not to break it and leave a part of it, and the tooth will remain in place longer due to the mischief of the root, causing the patient greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act as the ignorant lords do, who by their haste and bravery sometimes break a chariot, and never bring what we have mentioned; but they sometimes bring about any harm from this great disease through the roots that remain or through the chariot that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or vinegar and oil; and if bleeding comes forth, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one silences the teeth first, should be long points and large handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be large enough so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron, and be toothed for gripping.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the roots remain after pulling a tooth, you must put on the place cotton soaked in butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 While the shoulder joint is crushed, put the forceps called "algefri" inside, which resemble a beak for healing; and they should be shaped like a chisel on the inside. This is its form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tools, then you must expose the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as forceps, in this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Be large and thick so it does not break, and if the root jumps out with them, that is good; if not, help with all the instruments, as the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you aid with this instrument having two arms, in this shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and of this tool that appears like large pincers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool should not be breakable, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the wise master finds his own instrument by himself, according to what his work and the disease show, because there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach any instrument due to diversity in ailments; and if it breaks a cart or another bone where it should not, then it searches for the tools that are required, which I have told you, and assists with gestures, as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and firm to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but can hold and remove; then restore the place of medicines suitable for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, then apply all this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural shape and are misshapen, even in virginal women, you must know if the tooth is not born after the dent, and is not properly aligned, and cannot be treated or filed: then cut it off; and if it is erupting with the tooth, take this instrument which has the form of a small beak, sharp at the tip, made of iron;
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle of the chisel should be held often for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, file it with a small flat file as shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file used to make needles; and with the flat file grind the tooth little by little, so that it does not move too much while grinding; then flatten the end at any rasp, and if the tooth is very sharp and bites the tongue, you must grind away the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth are loosened by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press on them without them chattering, and you have cured them with binding medicines, it is of no use; they should be restrained with a gold thread, for silver threads become green and rot, but gold never changes; and the thread should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; if you see the teeth aligned, take the thread and double it between the two loose teeth, then put the forceps between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering up to the part where you started, and hold your hand gently but firmly, so that they do not move; and tie the thread at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then sew the shoulder bones with a needle and tweezers, and put them back between the healthy joint, and place it so that it does not pierce the tongue; then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the thread breaks, hold it in place with another thread; if it stays and serves thus for its entire duration, this is the shape of teeth and the form of the alignment of the two healthy joints and the two bones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out and is replaced back in its place, freshly and as we have said; let no one interfere who is not skilled and patient, and sometimes the shape of an animal bone is made and placed where it is missing, and it is tied as we have said, and remains for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 There is sometimes a ligament that comes under the tongue or is born thus, or due to accidental wound healing; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head still, and lift the tongue; then sew the nerve ligament wide enough until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or not, it is a deep wound, and sew the unguis and widen the one that is ligamented; and ensure that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is below; and when you have done this, raise the affected limb with warm water and oil, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and bind the patient's head each night so the limb cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And when blood discharge occurs, place it on the level of vitriol powder; and if it refuses to stay, cauterize with slow fire (slow-burning fire), which is good for this purpose; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of a faint color or black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it's declining to blenchor and there is moisture, then insert an uncine and make a small incision with a thin spatula from both sides; and if the wound doesn't heal at your treatment, apply vitriol powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your treatment until you remove all the pus; then apply a cold compress and let it heal with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes boils called "godath" come inside the throat, which are properly called "the two almonds". And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 If it is red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, likewise for the blood discharge; but leave it until it becomes ripe, and then you will divide it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of pale color again, and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check that the abscess is not hot and has been pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders be in alignment, and open his mouth wide and the sergeant takes hold of it between his hands, and presses the tongue under all the instrument, as shown here; and it should be made of silver or fine iron like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Keep pressing the tongue on the entire instrument and you see the abscess. Then take the hook and stick it into the almond, and pull it up more than you can; and draw any cloth away with it, then cover it with the instrument, forming something that resembles a fist. However, the chief are curved and one end to the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or brass:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool present, use pliers of this shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	Then when you have caught one of the almonds, take the other according to the same manner, and after incising, gargarize the patient with hot sharp and thin instruments, and if there is evacuation of blood, then gargarize the patient again with hot sharp and thin instruments, or scorches of pomegranates cooked or myrtle branches, and similar things, until the wound is cauterized; then let it heal completely; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat instead of the two almonds, if these appear, cut them in the same way as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And so I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside the throat, to wit, the abscess of small size; and had tightly closed all her throat, such that the woman could not exhale due to the constricted passage, nor eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had risen to two fingers above the two openings of the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 Then I immediately inserted it into one [the patient], afterwards pulled it forcefully and a large portion of the bone; afterwards I reset another fracture in the other shoulder, opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; then I inserted the bone again into these abscesses, and took a part of it, and no more blood came out except a little; and thus the woman was led from the throat, and began to drink cold water and then wine, and did not cease to cut down the abscess for a long time; and the abscess closed up again, filling the place that I had seen empty, until it became very large; then I tricked him and cauterized inside his throat; thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and let God do what He would with them afterwards.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the rectum protrudes to the outside and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and rounded, it is called "bladder".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is treated as we said in the division and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses have calmed down, and it is subtle, you should cut it; and if it is rounded and not long, and it is bloody or of pale color or black, you should make the incision for it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to the way that I have said, of its thickness and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue on the instrument as we have reminded before; then insert the probe into the bladder, pull it out, and cut it with the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two anuses.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cover any superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you do so more, it harms the voice and the word; and after the incision, use what was said in the incision of the II amandres, and heal it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 If the patient fears covering (it), then you must use an engine for the cauterization to allay his fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the method of cauterizing is with hot iron.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient must place his head in your lap, and then press his tongue against the instrument that was said in the chapter of cauterizing, and fix with hot live coal, so it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has hair or some substance that you can put medicine on, such as the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument entirely over the medicine on the uvula; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine but do not reach the throat or the pharynx; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it against the uvula, for about half an hour until you see it redden and the bites of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with all the cotton on top of the uvula, allowing the cotton to stick to the uvula; and repeat this process until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. If you need to start the cautery again using the medicine, do so, and after the cautery rinse around the uvula with cotton dipped in burr, clean what is around the medicine; wash with cold water and treat with gargarisms until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, not just cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this way, take camomile, yarrow, origanum, rue, and wormwood, and put them all together or some of them in one pot, add ashes, and make it boil; the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and have one vessel with a cover inside the pot according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the heads pushed into the mouth of the patient until the steam rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is made rotten; afterwards it often occurs, until the eye dries up, and ensure that you do not do this at the beginning of the abscess heat, for many things happen; and do not ever do this but at the decline of the abscess heat.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this is not present, take a canal and put an eggshell crack inside the head of the patient so that his mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell crack will not let the steam overheat the mouth, and it is good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often it sticks in the throat, bone or fish spine, or something else; therefore you should pull out what can be seen, and press the tongue against the sun until you see movement of the object; and if it does not open and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will expel the object. Or, the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cotton, or a radish root, or a small piece of dry bread; tie one thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; when it reaches the place, it will stick, and then you can pull it out. And if it does not come out as we have said, take a piece of wood according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and lift the head high; watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, so that nothing harms it or pushes the bone inward; it is better if the patient puts the instrument, because he can move it or the thing is easier to move; if he pushes it down, or pulls it out completely, keep the instrument equal until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	the vein of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the patient is cured without medication, as I have said in the division, by the use of medicines; and when it does not help at all, then look into the throat of the sick person towards the sun, because you press the tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the pus, pull it out very gently, or use subtle tweezers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that does not work, take a hairy rope and put it in the throat of the sick person, then insert or push into the throat the hot iron several times.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And let the patient drink water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, pour it in such a way that it flows down the throat and is swallowed, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the pus senses the water, let it fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it [the dislocated limb] does not fall as we have said, you should subdue the patient with anesthetic, at the instrument I mentioned in the uve fumigation; do this many times, for it will require much [treatment].
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The method of fumigation is that you take the pot or one containing charcoal, and cover it with a cloth perforated in the middle, and put the head of the instrument inside; then pour your fumigation into it, and make the patient hold the end of the tube in his mouth and close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape but comes only to his sinuses; and the sinuses will now open, and if it [the dislocated limb] does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient should suffer from thirst, and eat salty things and almonds, and drink nothing of water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument to treat the nose, is like scissors curved for entering the throat; and resembling the beak of a syringe, and it should have sharpness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see below its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many resemble an abscess, according to what comes after in this book from one and the other, and they differ in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways that one of them is similar, and when it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is by the joints that are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses of the head are different from those on the base, and abscesses in the shoulder blade are different from those that come at the joints; each should have its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced, until the swelling is moderate according to its completion; and if there are such that it must be pierced when they are ripe, but do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that come from joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when an abscess appears at the joints and is left until it bursts, inadvertently the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 For if an abscess is present at the main member and you delay the perforation until it becomes ripe, damage will be done to the main member; or if it is opened before it has ripened, this is harmful; nor should you pierce the abscess without complete digestion, except in the case of an abscess under the foundation which cannot pass through and be opened and a fistula forms, and cannot heal within a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time for perforation of the abscess that is ripe according to completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the subsiding of fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the opening and narrowing of the abscess's head, and other signs; and you should make the perforation where it depends more on the abscess, and where it has opened up; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that are swollen, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a charred place, it is good to leave the perforation until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 If you pierce it before that, the body will flow with fluid from it and will be filled with much pus; and by chance, the lips may harden and it may become sealed within.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess that has been pierced according to the size of the body, as required by the limbs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 It is necessary that you make small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where the scab must be shaved, covered; when it has become as thin as a cloth and is moist, it is necessary to do as with babies: and if there are those that have been cut into three angles, and those from which one covers as with the fruit of the myrtle, like angina abscesses; and if there are those where a round incision has been made, and other similar cuts and appearances, it is necessary to cover them.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 One who has no head, like a superficial abscess, you must pierce it fully; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, you should not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing incorrectly; do this repeatedly, gradually, as much as needed, until the pus is gone; likewise, if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying a child, or small children, or elderly people with decrepitude.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 The pus jumps out at times with the release of the pus, by chance the patient may die, and you should not worry.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, approach this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, drain the wound, and observe if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a large abscess, bring threads of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess and there is much pus, you must insert a thread in every one so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, you must fill it with old cotton or linen gauze without moisture, and bind it for three days; then open it, and cure it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and linen cloth, dampen it, and place it on the wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the bleeding persists, provide care and treatment, and apply the powders mentioned in this book in the hands, and if it is a cold season, and the wound or abscess is very nervous, you should place hot tents and damp cloths on it; if it is summer, and the wound is fatty, place damp cloths on it with cold water and oil, or cold water and cool oil, until the third day, as we have said; then open the abscess, drain it, and treat it, as necessary, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to approach treatments for abscesses, and now here is the chapter.
des soros	on les doibt traiter par cautere de feu, et si c'est li soros qui est gros ou si c'est en estete, il faut les fistraire ou les aignorer avant; et s'il sont durs et ne puissent pas fistreier, alors les coupez en peus et empoignez le tueu par dessous la poix, et mettez feu au cautere, et on les brande comme il se peut, et ains qu'il soit bien chauffez, pesez le cautere et mettez l'en une vase d'eau, et le tirez hors du tueu qui est oste; et lors que li soros seront toutes ensemeies, si les clavetiez ains qu'il se refroidissent, si com il covient.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses on the head, it is our practice to use linen cloths, as a gardener with a gourd, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that have grease and moisture like blisters, and there are those that are hard and rough at the edges without any doubt that they do not oppose the arteries.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is that you probe with every instrument called "entomoisoir," which gives rise to the following form, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they make a long incision through it.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is drained, they scrape without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, because it returns quickly if left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment (if present); otherwise in vinegar and lime, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain will heal by the third day.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then continue the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, as long as you know that it does not heal too slowly; then treat the wound with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess is swollen with pus, press it according to this shape, longwise; and throw out your onions, and remove the scabs from all parts, and apply all your care to draw out the pus where it lies; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And similarly do for the abscess if it is pockmarked, and cut and treat as I told you before.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And the incision on the abscess becomes moist, it is lighter, for there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And in some of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and from those I cut open an old woman's abscess; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one were to cut into it with any tool, one would make as great a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or heads coming from places other than children's heads and the roots of the ears, they should be opened for as long as necessary depending on the location, to allow pus to drain out; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this abscess occurs at the neck, under the jaw, and in the groin area, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they are large and connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 Each scrofula is properly within its side, like the abscess of the neck and the abscess at the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities in these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the one that you see with a good position to be touched, and resembles the color of the body, silent in every part and not pierced at the neck nor at the artery nor the conduit, and not penetrated; then you should cut it from above, peel off each part, and place the two lips of the incision as close together as you can if you have to, as we have said in abscesses at the head; and draw it out slowly, and be sure that you do not pierce the nerve or the vein, and do not use too much force, let your hand not tremble, and look not too far ahead, so as not to pierce what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or the artery and it does not let you finish, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that stop blood, and hold the wound closed; leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the wound is not clotted, return to your work until you complete it; then examine if there remain small scrofulas, if so, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofulas wound, it is not necessary to cut that scrofulas at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang out, without harm; then apply old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you excise the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you close the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no more superfluous material remaining due to the largeness of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it and draw pus, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas that have superfluous material, pierce there where the opening is wide; and pierce it in the same way as the one mentioned above, in the direction of the flow, then bring in tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrodes what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply an ointment healing charcoal until it heals.
de squinance	If you make a bloodletting from the artery, then you must bind the veins that are near so that the bleeding does not continue, and close the wound with clean cloths.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the size of the throat, but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have quinsy, it is required that the throat slit called "epiglottis" should be opened; and no help should be given by these [affected areas], because all veins and the entrance of the sickness are in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the tonsil, it is required to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it below three circles or four small slits through the middle, between the two circles or by the size of the split not in the cartilage; and these muscles are capable of being sectioned at the epiglottis's cut such that there is no cartilage. And the vessels are long from here onwards.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 If the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat completely, then cuts the cartilage until it reaches the trachea; and avoids the blood vessels if you see anything, and then cut the split as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe which bursts through the broken place, and by the absence of voice; leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed in which doubt of strangulation exists, bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it closed with care, taking care to avoid the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Abu'l-Qasim says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged dead, and the bird pecks out his eyes.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then compress the windpipe because the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, thus guarding against death; and for this reason, the ancients would leave the wound open until the sickness had passed, which happens in 3 or 4 days. And then they would command to sew up the wound and heal it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 A maiden took the knife and stuck it in her throat, piercing part of the windpipe's channel; I was called to heal her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and discovered blood coming out of it, and that it had not opened or led the vein except through the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I quickly sewed up the wound, healed it until it was healthy; and nothing happened to the maiden but her voice turned red, and she recovered after that; for this reason, I say in such a situation, have no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large one, colored like a grape, and it occurs mostly in women; and it is according to two kinds: natural and accidental; where natural has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental is according to two kinds, of which one is similar to fatty nodes, and the other kind is similar to an abscess that comes from us through arteries; there should be fear, and it is not advisable to operate on it without force except in small ones, and prove and search for everything at the intromission: if you find it similar to fatty nodes, and does not open anywhere, hit it as we hit the lymph nodes, and pull off its entire covering, if there is any; and enclose it tightly, and cure it as needed, until it becomes perfectly healthy.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of ours are, which I will say all their similarities; and now it is necessary that I say the entire difference between notch and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	A dislocation is characterized by heat and fever persisting until the inflammation has passed, and then the purulence is complete; afterwards, the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 A notch has no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the sinus (sin), which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and it begins in the same way as a boil, and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, either fatty or moist, and most of their colors are as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the care of the sick, that you examine and test first all the instruments called "entromissoire," according to its shape or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 The manner of inquieting the abscesses from ours is that you take or a more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has perforated the core; then you should extract the intruder, and pay attention to not let it escape.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs out from the abscess and it changes color, treat it as I have said for other abscesses; but if no more moisture comes out after opening the abscess, know that it is full, then make an incision in the form of a cross, grasp it with tweezers, gently scrape it from both sides and pull the skin or coat that you are pulling safely with the thread; and if you cannot pull it safely, then cut it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If nothing remains, the pus will return multiple times; and if a little pus remains but does not bother you, apply some corrosive powder to the wound, close the wound, place something warm over the abscess to treat it, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the pus is large, cut the edges of the wound twice, and heal the raw flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is swollen in contrast or other cases where you are forced to act quickly, use the leech of vitriol powdered, leave it for 2 or 4 days until the wound starts to heal, and let the evacuation of blood stop; then return to treating the part that was left with new dressing.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Behold the forms of the probing instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are also three corners which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula; and they are similar to needles used to sew shoes, and they are made of citron wood, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and they are more skilled at piercing through black planks to encircle the openings of fistula; and they are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wound's width.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of tumors resemble much, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are tumors with two humps in three ways; and there are tumors with three humps, which also have three shapes; and there are tumors with two humps and one hump only, and they also have three shapes; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The tips of these [objects] that are cut are sharp, and those who do not cut them only from one side, so as to avoid striking the vein or nerve; and these insertion points are closed with alum and bound in several ways, so that the patient does not feel it when opening abscesses; and they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are not used anywhere except in charnut [hard, dry] places such as legs, arms, breasts, and anuses, and sometimes a smaller one is made, resembling fistula cauteries, according to this shape, for bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put to the place that stops bleeding from veins, arteries, and sometimes returns according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 At times, the breasts of some men swell when they begin to decay, until they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must do so according to this form of the line b. up to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then scrape off the fat, apply medicine to the wound with soothing char, then bring together the two lips of the wound to stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks downwards and is flattened due to its size, as happens with women, if it becomes two breasts, cut them in two at the top, as if they were two similar splits; so that one is attached to the other at the end of each one, making the larger line contain the smaller according to this form from b. up to g; then scrape the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what has been said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it digests the remaining fat, then cure it until it is drained.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses of buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the buttocks are cases of hard scrofula where there is moisture contained within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line 'b' up to the line 'g': [This part doesn't need translation as it is a technical instruction about making a surgical cut.]
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire bowel in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula (or scrofulous lesions), then make incisions in it as we have said before in scrofula incisions, and if the wound swells, apply a cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The cutting of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is open and the skin is stuck together above it, there are often abscesses and the same happens with a burst vein and an abscess; and when one recognizes it by the artery, the abscess will be long in depth; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels strained; and when it is for the vein, it turns red on the surface; and it is foolish to cut such an abscess, especially when it is under the nails and angles and at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	1.
