It is necessary to remove the iron cure, and also the one who has a head injury must be treated in the same way; and in the one whose artery swells on top of the skin, make an incision through the leather (skin) lengthwise; then open the abdomen as usual, carefully separate the artery from the tendons, until it is exposed; then insert a needle beneath it, and pierce it all the way to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then press the area between the two bands with an instrument until the swelling subsides, and separate the abscess; then apply the cure with a bow until the tendon cries out (indicates pain); then treat it with ointment as needed, until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to an opening in a vein, you must mark the area that you can from the abscess all over the skin, then insert the needle beneath the area that you are holding in your hand, pierce it, and tie it with a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or with a ligature of one of the two ends of the thread; and if you doubt whether the threads will hold, insert another needle through all the threads beneath the incision of the first needle, and tie them in four places; then press the abscess so that the excess subsides, then press the excess fat and leave what is tied; then put a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply cures of tents (bandages) and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	from abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses can occur in the artery and vein, so too do abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this often happens with shoulders and thumbs and in all places where there are joints, and it is the great abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many dispositions causing pain; and when it is squeezed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely in the body, but under the skin; and it is quite quiet in all places, and does not go forward or backward, neither up nor down, and one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps contraction will occur; and one who is on the head or on the forehead, stretch the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and strike at its root; if it is large, open it with an incision, scrape it, then remove the bone and close the wound with stitches, and let it heal until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	Large lumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Occasionally, it occurs in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "funge," resembling mushrooms; its roots are subtle, and its heads are large; they have both small and very large ones; I saw a man who had two bellies that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were cut open, and moisture ran out of it continuously.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed it and found that one was 18 oz., and the other was 6 lb., and in the operation during incision, you must look at whether the patient is moist; if the color of the artery is pale and moist with a subtle root, take the spatula wide open and have the fire cautery ready for it.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in the thigh there often comes too much discharge of blood, and if it flows out, hurry up and cauterize [the wound]; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron incision, take well-made thread, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then pull it tight, and do not stop pulling on the thread until it stops the discharge, and feels labor pains; and if the roots are thick, be careful to cauterize only the center, but you can easily cauterize half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be sure to not cauterize the tendon which is of a dark color and poor sensation and milky sight.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an enlarged abscess, and I will come to the treatment of syphilis afterward.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts out
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or split in the body, and it is on the belly and among some of the buboes, as happens in other routes, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries, according to what is before, or due to inflammation; and if it is through the route of the bubo and the exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	If it is caused by the outburst from the intestines, then it is more various. When you press it with your hands and it recedes, it returns again, and sometimes if it is sutured, it grows greatly at the entrance of the bath and due to hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and easily opened when pressed with your hand, do not force it; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and filled according to a certain amount; and if it is due to inflammation, it is soft to the touch, and the procedures are such that you look to see whether the appearance is due to the blood of an artery, or a vein, or inflammation.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 It is necessary to let the treatment rest.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is from the intestine or the abdomen, you must instruct the patient to fasten their side and be extended straight, then press around the swelling; then command him to lie on his back between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with a spatula, then stretch half of the abscess above with a large spoon; then tie it around with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the sutures be tight; then open half of the stretched abscess over the thread, and insert your finger, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught by the thread, remove it, and push the intestine to the opposite side of the abdomen; and if you find a swelling, take it with the spoon, and cut off the superfluidity; and if the artery or vein oppose you, go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two sharp points, and insert the needles around what you have made in cross shape that you are going to pierce; then hold the abscess in four leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as it is, and let the flesh rot by itself; or cut it when it becomes soft and can be pierced, then cure it as required, and seal the abscess as we have said; and extract the pus or the moisture that you find, then cure the place as required, and suture the place.
dou chancre	draw the boil
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of boils and how to treat them with medicine, and how to handle the cure with iron; and we will say that boils begin in the armpit, and great caution is needed in its treatment; and the ancients said that when a boil is in a place where it can be shaved like a boil that is on the breast or thigh, and in similar places, and it must all be removed when it is at the beginning; but when it is large and old, it should not be approached, for I have never known anyone to heal it; nor has anyone healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the surgeries, when they are in place and can be removed as we have said, are that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him urinate if he has manifest repletion, then prepare the patient. That is, boil a clean linen cloth or bandage to perform the surgery; then pour your unguents or salve over the sore, and the entire head of it, and the bone from all sides, leaving nothing behind; let the blood flow freely and press well on the place with your hand or something, and if the discharge of blood makes you oppose the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize it until the wound is scorched; then treat it with another cure until it heals.
de ydropisie	The translation for this line would be "of hydropisia." Hydropisia refers to a medical condition in which there is excessive accumulation of water or fluid in the body tissues, specifically in the abdominal cavity.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have said in the division the resemblances of edema, and in what manner the collection of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure that is done with medicines, and that which is cured with iron: only these two resemblances should be excluded; namely tympanites and hypophysis, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this resemblance of edema called "edemas" with medicines, and the cure does not help, observe if the patient is weak or if he has another disease besides edema, such as dropping water and similar things; do not use iron in this case, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong constitution, and he only has edema, and he does not have any other disease besides that, and he is neither too young nor too old, then operate as follows: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the assistant presses the abdomen pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder; then take the curved spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut through its second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be pierced not too deeply so that it does not reach the intestines when it is inserted, and it should not be blistered; then check if the urinary bladder is inflamed towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision below the third rib to the right of the navel; and if it is due to liver disease, the incision should be on the left side of the third rib; and if it is due to constipation, it should be on the right, and the patient should not lie down on the incision so that fluids do not run to that weak place; then pierce the skin with the instrument, push it in, and withdraw your hand to the spatula between the skin and the bladder as much as the size of a nail or thereabouts; then pierce the bladder until the spatula reaches the water level, which is the bladder's neck, then pull it out, and put this instrument where it is shown in the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it resembles a silver needle, thin and made of lead or light thread, and at the part below the small wound; where it pierces through from one side, there are three holes; and from another part, two, and one from the other; and the head is cut like a feather quill, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes carve with their pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 Above the head is the opening, so that when the instrument comes to the water, you should now press up on the instrument; empty then the middle or third part, because if you empty more than necessary in this hour, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit due to the weapon, or they will fall to the ground, or come close to death; but empty according to its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the strength of the patient indicate, and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now by the cauterization that stops the flow which I have spoken about, namely, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument on another day, if you see the patient suffering this, and draw out a little water; do this every day, and be careful not to leave it but a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and leave him much water, treat him with sepulture or hot sand, and with much sweat or bath and in the sun, and anoint him with wine; and treat him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize the stomach, liver, and spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born who have no foreskin or whose foreskins are small and not in the right place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary that you make a very thin incision in all spittle-like places according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then put the thin foreskin of wood on it, and hold and keep it in place for three or four days until he wants to urinate, then remove the closure, let him urinate, and then replace it; and in case, there is no need, because the urine that comes out does not leave the closure closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 For the person whose wound is small, the treatment with a cup made of lead, as we have said, will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those without a wound in their place are bled, because no one is born who has a wound on the head of the penis, for they cannot urinate before lifting their penis; and cannot engage due to this reason as the matter cannot reach the vagina, and it is an evil disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of work is that the patient lies on his back with his head raised slightly like the shaft of an arrow, and his buttocks likewise, so that his genitals are in a hole, as required; and be careful of blood leakage which often occurs, and if it happens, apply a pressure to stop the bleeding, and heal the wound until it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis ulcers
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albath appears in the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly skin; there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you should treat them with a .i. oncine (once) of subtle substance, then scrape them off and cleanse thoroughly, afterwards apply moist cotton in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diaphinicon ointment until it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, of a greenish-yellow color and foul smelling, then you must apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have scraped it, and if the ulcer is on the shaft of the penis, and has both parts within the skin and parts outside, then you must first remove the ulcer that is inside; and when it is sewn up, you should treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you treat the penis, it is not certain that the testicles will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come into the penis and its surrounding area; then you must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from the skin of pomegranates and walnuts, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if there is discharge of blood, bring the lunar cautery as follows:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cauteries assist each other in the following way: for discharge of blood and corruption; and if the testicles of the penis are corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you bring or lead from the penis a cane made of wood, and make the patient urinate; and when the hairs appear at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to injury or abscess, then it is necessary to shave it with an instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and release the testicles from all sides; and if it is a difficult matter to speak of this, it is necessary to shave it with a thin blade, a little distance from the head of the penis and the pubic hair; then press gently between them, and put a fine linen cloth dipped in cold water on top. It should not appear immediately.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the same as other wounds in terms of continuation; however, when we perform this work of our own free will and specifically on children, it is necessary that we do the best job and make it as easy to heal as possible.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for it is not in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greater part of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around one day, and with great force, and in a novacule; however, there were those who were careful because there are two layers, and by chance if one above is cut and delayed, the one below will be damaged.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now cover it with copper, and the pain is doubled; and at the amputation which is deep in the limb, the point of the member is not secure; and at the amputation of the nail by chance the iron escapes, and ruins the work, and many times there is no need for amputation and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the amputation which is made all through the thread of iron I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the saw cuts exactly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Whenever you press your hand, you should cut it evenly in all its thickness; but the edge should be well narrowed around the skin; and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not bind him except to tie a thread around the rod only, and then let him play in any way that you can; then let it be between your hands straight, and replace the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them nor any tool; then push your hand against the rod and blow or cough, and draw it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it well of the filth assembled there, then tie the joint signet with a double thread, then tie below one thread to another cord; and hold it by the second knot to the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two cords, then untie the thread quickly and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood flow freely as it wishes, for this is the cure; and put powder on top and on top the powder stick with a little cooked egg white mixed with fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with other medicine until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tender and pierced, and they should be equal in size to the knuckles.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the amputation is when the cartilage within is cut; therefore, you must stretch it with your nail so that the joint becomes abscessed; and strike it evenly. And if you cannot hold it with your nail, take tongs, and then strike it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it exceeds three days, and that which is beneath the penis becomes swollen, let it be until the abscess subsides, and scrape lightly; then strike it as you can move it, and be careful not to damage the penis.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with things that are submerged in a wound of powder, as we have said or treated powders, and if you strike it with excessive care, and it goes beyond [the limit], it will not harm; therefore, treat it as we have said until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, frozen blood, pus, charnee (flesh-like substance) or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that the retention is caused by a stone which is lodged at the neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient be bowed over his knees; and his feet should be placed on the back, and he should extend his abdomen from the upper part of his back, and hold the patient as tightly as possible; then the neck of the bladder must be compressed at the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is relieved; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you administer extraction using an instrument called "siringue", whose shape is as follows: made of thin and light silver cane, like a bird's feather; and its nozzle should be one palm and a half long, and be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the urine issue is that you take a double thread, tie one end to the top of the linen or cotton cloth and push the other end into the syringe; then tie off the excess linen and push it up to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a chair, and rub the bladder and penis with oil moistened with warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base of the penis, then double the penis over the syringe towards the anus; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and have the patient feel the urine coming out until it reaches the empty space, this should not be done in any other order because the conduit through which it goes is twisted; then wind the thread around the linen cloth and the urine follows the linen, then pull it out, and straighten the urine; then reinsert the syringe as many times as necessary until the bladder is empty, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	On the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorches or blood comes in the bladder, or pus is assembled there and you see it distill liquids and medicines, then use all the instruments called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and if it has three openings: two of one kind, and one of another, as you see; and the head of the vein should be closed in such a way that the medicine can stop the flow without addition, if it can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see medicines thrown into the bladder, place the head of the casket in the moisture, and draw along with it; if you draw out the moisture with the casket, then forcefully press along with it; it will enter the casket, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle enema used to cleanse the bladder: here it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or iron, and the head is higher; beneath it lies the breast or the liver; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture that you use to clean the bladder, then form a double thread from two strings, and heat the moistened wool on fire; then insert the chief of the plaster into the sheath, then hold your hand above the bladder with all the moisture facing upwards, until the patient feels that the moistened wool has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, and puncture it roundly; then push a strong thread through these holes, assemble the circle like a thimble, fill it with oil and moisture and water, place it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the methods of stone and its extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone caused by the rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate in size; and in the bladder, and in the vein; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder occurs more often with children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder, resembling urine in its subtlety; it opens the narrow passages, irritates the patient's organ, pricks it many times, and then binds it; and much of these leaps cause the foundation to weaken; and the healing of children is easy until they reach 4 years old, but it is very difficult in the elderly, and it is a moderate illness for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to treatment, it is first necessary to purify the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes obstructs seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet, bend and move him downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and ascends sometimes towards the top; then make him sit between your hands prepared, his hands below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining downwards; then press and touch inside; if you feel the stone within the space, hurry now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall at the touch, moisten your left hand with oil, if the patient is male, or use your thumb, if the patient is female and of full age; then push on the foundation and press the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, squeeze it towards the neck of the bladder; then press above with your finger, and push it outwards in the direction where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch out his right hand upward and remove the skin that is under the testicles in the area where you make the cut; then insert the spatula spreading, which gives it its shape.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it should be made between the one that is located between the cheekbones and the base of the skull, not in the middle but on the left side of the nose; and it should be straight through the bone, and your hand should be against the base or foundation, and the opening should be wide at the exit, and narrow within, according to the size of the bone, not too large; possibly the pressure from the hand that is against the base will cause it to jump out without effort; and know that there may be a bone or an angle, and margins: if it is grated, then it should come out; and if it is rounded, like a bean, and round, the opening will be easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 If it is angular or has margins, make the opening larger; and if it does not come out, you must strain with pliers that are like a chisel at the head, to straighten the bone so that it does not splinter; or push in a thin curved instrument into the head; and if you cannot manipulate it thus, enlarge the opening slightly, and scrape it with vitriol; and if there is more than one bone, push the largest towards the bladder first, then hit, pull out, and the smaller ones after if there are any.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 If it is very large, it must be made larger by making a bigger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For the patient, there are two possible outcomes: death or urine constantly coming out because the wound cannot heal; but you should still try to draw it or break it with pliers until you can pull it apart piece by piece; and when you have finished your work, you should fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and bind it up, and cover it with a damp cloth in oil and vinegar, or in oil and cold rose water and cold water, to soothe the abscess that is hot; then make the patient rest on his neck, and do not undo the bandages until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you undo it (the bindings), immerse the wound well in oil and water, then apply the ointment "dyafinicon" and "basilicon" until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 If abscesses and ulcers come into the wound and there is blood coagulation in the bladder, and the urine is retained, which is known to be harmful without passing with urine: then press your hand on the wound, and drain that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder and spread it; then lift the wound from moisture and pus, and help in all ways you know until it heals; and it is necessary that all the herbs you use to treat it, that you bind the two legs together, and apply the medicines on top of it.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the wound is small and it is led by the penis and pierced through, and urine cannot pass out; cure it as I am about to say, that you cut it many times, and excise the cut by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already experienced this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod in the shape as follows and sharpened at four angles, pointed on one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the thread and tie it around the stone's shaft so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the awl gently into the shaft; then turn the awl slowly towards your hand in the stone, little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it bursts and jumps with the urine, the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie the thread around the stone beneath and another one above, then push the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from women's stones (kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that a stone is in the womb of women, and if it ever occurs, it is a great distress for the cure, and it is forbidden for four reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman skilled enough to examine her, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is deeper than the stone of the man, which requires a more profound incision and great fear arises. If it becomes necessary to do so, you must take a midwife who knows, and if one cannot find her, cast a subtle eye; and present a wise matron in the affairs of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to perform the incision of the stone; and pay close attention that the woman is a virgin. Then it must be commanded to push her pelvis or bottom and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she should confine it under her pelvis, and you should command her to push her pelvis or hold onto the patient, and press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If found, it must be moved gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike above the stone in the root of the thigh near the middle of the bone, where the stone is moved around; and do not move the finger above or below the stone, and let it be small at first; then push the hand into the lower abdomen, if you feel the stone pressing the wound so that the stone can issue forth, and know that there are many types of stones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 know the appearances to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the bone is protruding, put broken vitriole on it and hold it for an hour until the bone stops bleeding; then return to your work, as long as the arrowhead is still in, and have the tools I told you about when extracting an arrowhead for assistance in your work; and if the bone continues to protrude, and it is the artery that has been cut, put powder on the area and hold with straps and bandages, do not start again, leave the arrowhead and do not draw it out, or the patient may die; then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wounds have closed, return to your work, until the arrow is expelled.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	An aquous hernia is nothing but a gathering of moisture or pus, which is beneath the bladder that contains the egg; and it is called "pus," and sometimes it is specifically in the egg's membrane itself, if one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the bladder between the pus we have mentioned; and this does not happen except without any reason.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the growth of this hernia is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and the matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 Sometimes it happens that a blow occurs on the kidneys, and this moisture takes on various colors: either a color that declines to yellow, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and this often happens; these are signs for recognizing this assembly, for if it is as white as we have said, it indicates an abscess, the size of an egg yolk, and do not open the kidneys, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very fabric [of the abscess], it is believed that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin and the yellow matter [pus], one can feel it well; therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you should probe with a blunt instrument, from which its form is as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, judge what is inside based on the probe that comes afterwards.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we treat [the abscess] with iron, it is necessary that the patient be anesthetized to our ability and the fullness of his body; then he lies on his back, on a thing slightly raised, and covers him with many layers of cloth; then he lies on his left side, and commands the assistant to stand at right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the shoulder; then take the spatula flat, and strike the skin between them along its length until reaching the point below the handle, and ensure that the incision is straight in slicing the skin until white pus, and remove it delicately according to our ability; then pierce the pus completely with water at a large opening, and drain all the water, and then insert your fingers, and stretch the pus upward; do not touch the ribs, but only the pus; strike the entire side of it carefully, for if you do not strike it correctly, the pus will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the pus; then sew together the two sides of the skin near the shoulder with a stitch, and treat [the wound] as other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to bind the vessels that are suspended (attached) with caution, fearing the release of blood; afterwards, cut through the suspension and extract the egg, treating it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an ulcer is assembled in two parts joined together (these are the branches), strike the other part as you did the first equally, then suck out the blood, and put damp linen wetted in rose oil into the wound; and put outside another damp linen wetted in vinegar and oil, and put over the two ends, and put over them doubled fabrics, and tie it all with a rope according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take the two fabrics, and use them of damp linen according to this shape and sewn together in the belt of the arms, and one of the ends takes hold beneath the foundation up to the back, and the other at the hilt part; and the other end on the two angles, and bind all together in the loop of the bandage; and sometimes the cautery ramification is used in place of iron cut, and it is that you take the cautery knife-like, and strike the skin of the ends, and let them be heated as we have said, so that the white pus contained by the ulcer is exposed; then take the cautery according to this shape, and perforate the pus with onion-shaped holes, and scrape it with this sharp cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the blow in all ways that you can, as long as you are heating it; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg (meaning: yolk); and know that this work is more effective; and pay attention to the correct flow of blood, and do the incisions carefully; and if anything happens contrary to this, or abscess or flow of blood or something else, cure what happens contrary to it, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is afraid and does not want to endure this work because of its horribility, administer perforation as I told you before; and it is that when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that a pimple has formed in the place, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below with a spatula wide enough; and make the perforation along the length of the body; let the punctures be large so that all the pus can flow out; then put cotton over the area and hold it, allowing the remaining pus to drain out, until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the pus to flow out from the opening of the wound, you must insert a pen or the instrument used for draining the pus of those suffering from dropsy (meaning: edema), whose form was mentioned before; enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the pus will return, and will be collected after 6 months or more; and when it is collected as mentioned before, and in this way the patient's days will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the kidneys
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the section of this treatise, many fear various dispositions, which is why it seems to me that it would be better to leave it [the disposition] as it is; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Then many abscesses come from the body, and similarly from the joints; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is about an overabundance of acidic and watery matter that is spread to the kidneys or from impact; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the body; it does not have pain, but is a severe abscess; and occasionally there are pus-filled, hard and piercing abscesses with such color, and sometimes comes from new arteries or swelling of veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from new arteries, it is known by the hot abscess position, when you press on it with your hands; and it should not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 One who is swollen with the vein is known by his disposition at the expression of the touch of the thumbs; and he can do well the incision on this appearance, and on other sores; and it is that you cut the core of the joints, then is the egg in high, and the string of the white pus, and delivers the suspension from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already soft with these sores born, then you must draw out the egg and crush it; and if it is swollen in the white pus, or in that which is within the bladders, you must deliver all that tenderness and crush it thoroughly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the hernia is at the rear end, you should cut it all out and extract the egg as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is done, apply the wound with moistened linen in rose oil and wine, then heal it with other treatments until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the kidneys
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enclosed by a covering resembling a boil, with the softening of the joints; and the patient groans heavily as he goes; and the cure for this disease is dangerous in the same way that this was previously mentioned, and we will tell you its treatment, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then place the suspension irons (or stirrups) below the knees against your thighs, at all the places near the thighbone; mark them with the master, and stretch them out fully; then strike the handle of the cautery wide across the thighbones until they are exposed, and then cut off the skin from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then insert a double-threaded needle there, and tie it to the first joint where the vein appears, and tie it straight to the other joint; then strike them exactly, according to the length of the body, and release the corrupted humors; then treat the wound as you would a broken bone, so that no blood flows from any of the thighbones; for this is not harmful, and if all the thighbones have veins, tie the thighbones to them all; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the veins, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sifac
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The occurrences of this condition are due to the incision or extension on the abdomen in the part of the inguinal region, because the intestines descend from that wound towards one of the kidneys; and this wound is either the incision or the extension of it, and these two types of injuries occur for many reasons such as percussion, jumping, falling, lifting heavy weights, and similar things; and the signs when it is the inguinal extension are that it happens gradually over a long time, not suddenly; and the abscesses are equal towards the end, because the inguinal region follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is of the section of the dislocation, are that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, under the skin near, and this is due to the outflow of the intestine and the body turning away from the dislocation.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines come out through the hernia, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, therefore it is necessary to escape from them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 The method of treatment is that you instruct the patient to push back the intestine inside with their hand towards the wound if they can reach it; then hold the abdomen on top, and spread the thighs; then open the inguinal region above, and cut all the skin from the kidneys longwise; then insert your index finger into the gap between the skin and the inguinal region, and locate the testicle that is under the skin, in the area between the white inguinal region and the scrotum, and between the two testicles; and separate what is behind the testicle and between the scrotum; then move the index finger to the side of the kidney towards the left hand, and pull the testicle away from the entire inguinal region towards the back; and instruct the assistant to stretch the testicle upwards, and disconnect what is in front behind the ligament; and look for signs if the intestine is wrapped around or the hard white inguinal region, and if you find anything, push it into the abdomen below; then take a large-needle with thick thread made of 10 strands, and insert it into the back part of the inguinal region, after the skin; then sew the stitches that appear from the thread, until there are four threads; then arrange them in the shape of a cross, and sew the inguinal region, which is under the skin of the kidneys, with a strong ligament of two parts; then sew the stitches made from the thread, and make sure no servants who nurse it can enter into it, unless the abscess does not come out; and tie the ligament as before, leaving a long distance of one finger's width for the inguinal region that is under the kidney skin; then sew the rest according to the roundness that the testicle carries; then cut in the area that is under the skin of the kidneys, until it is corroded and swollen, as we have said before; then apply moistened linen to the wounds, and apply the ligament that we have mentioned.
