Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the whites are cauterized as we have said, after the incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 This happens many times, and leave the ligament until it chooses to slip out; if it delays in falling, it should be softened with hot water, and place what has been said on it until it slips out; then cure the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I never saw anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like a graft joining the bone, in this way you tie the vessels, after cutting them lightly from below; then break it in half, and treat the abscess with what I have said, until the vessels grow; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes there comes a hernia in the groin, as we have said, and do not open any of the intestines at the anus, and if some do open, it is too little, and repair it hourly; and yet even if it stays too long in this place, the wound or phlegm forms there where the intestines are opening; and this happens due to the extension of the phlegm which is in the groin, as we have said, for it is stretched, then softened and swollen are the muscles and opened; and it is cured by cautery, as I have told you before; and sometimes it is healed by iron in this way: and the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then break the inflamed hernia swelling from the side according to the size of three fingers; and pull out the phlegm that is under the skin that surrounds it, then take the ram and put it on the exposed phlegm; and press it at the belly, then cut the two visible phlegms around the ram head, and cut one and the other; then pull out the ram head, and do not cover or stretch the phlegm or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the intestines hernia; then cure it by wound remedy.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads (sutures), if it becomes infected and heals the wound, let it remain until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The fistula (li sifac) is closed, and it has no appearance in the wound, and the cauterization is performed in this place, and it is closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin around the eyes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the eyes becomes soft in some men, because the charms that are inside are softened and it is visible; and when one wants to heal it, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their back, and you bandage the softened skin on top of the natural skin; then bring together the two lips to a stitch, and if you see, sew first the excess skin that is softened with four or five stitches firmly; then bandage between the stitches, and heal as other wounds, until it is healed, and stitch the thread.
dou chastrement	The punishment or correction (of a patient)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that castration is mentioned in our law, and for this reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: the first is that masters should answer when asked about castration and its cure; and the second, because we often have need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and pigs and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 Therefore, I say that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the castration done by attraction, we make the animal sit in warm water until its scrotum becomes soft and then hold it with our hand until it is settled and no longer feels anything.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 From the castration by cutting: it is necessary that you mark the animal, and you press the hide of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the restrainer, and strike above each testicle where you have cut, when you have skinned them properly; leave no small piece of skin or subtle skin that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is dried out as opposed to the one made by attraction, because at the attraction something may remain from the testicles, which makes the animal desire lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites (intersex individuals)
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism is according to the two ways of humans: one way is that there is an opening between the two testicles as in the figure of female nature with hair, and sometimes it urinates in court.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other method is in women, and it has above the hilt like a rod and they pierce it.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the cure for a man and a woman is that you cut all the surrounding tumors and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine jumps through the skin of the scrotum, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	The translation for this line is:
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Tumor is a tumor adjacent to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have one as big as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 You must stain the excess of the tumor with your hand or onions and cut it lightly; do not go too deep so blood does not come out, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed; and for another tumor that grows at the mouth of the anus, and farts and breaks through, and is like a cow's womb, and therefore called by the ancients "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 It must be cut as we have said before, and it should be cured until it is healed.
de erratique	From erratic [or wandering]
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 If the nature of a woman is not perceived or if it is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to disease that has come upon her; or it is by artificially joined male organ, or too thick or thin sperm, and it is made completely in the vagina, or in the costumes, or under them, or wherever it may be; and they must avoid conceiving, and give birth, and unfortunately allow the flowers to develop; and the recognition of this is by observing the discharge from the vagina.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the discharge approaches, it may be in your hand or at your side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is a subtle wound that is close to the liver, hurry and do this: place your two index fingers together, and have her lie on her back with her legs spread apart; then form the two livers as the subtle wound is rounded, and let the openings be wide; then take linen, moisten it in oil, and place it over the area, and make him lie down at home for each day so that he cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the wound is hard and thick, you should cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the opening is filled with pus, suspend it with onion and cut it; have ready the medicines that stop bleeding, such as garlic, dragon's blood, incense, and many eggs; then provide a large reed pipe, so that the wound cannot heal; let it be long-lasting, and provide a tent of dry linen; then cure other wounds until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when a child is born in marriage, it should be covered according to this manner, unless abscesses are swollen.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 To the swollen abscess that is within marriage, one should not make any attempt to touch it.
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids [or Piles]
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without cort (corticosteroid) treatment is customary, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn into piles; and we have said in the division their similarities, and signs, and I will tell you here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are fully formed in marriage, and cannot be felt, are not cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those at the mouth of the sore, which can be felt, are those who can be healed.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then heat the tongs at the anvils, and put it on its roots, then sprinkle medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then place her feet to the opening for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and grenadine bark and ivy leaves, and then prepare barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and apply the paste on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it stops bleeding, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If it doesn't stop bleeding, make tourniquets at the back and at the breasts without wounding them; then take linen, wet it in the juice of onions or juniper with old wine, and apply it to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess rests, heal the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a hawk's beak, so it must be covered as I said in the ointment recipe; and then it should be treated until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	emorroidal openings (of the anus)
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscess come in marriage, such as boils and hard abscesses, herpes, scabs, fissures, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Therefore, I must say in this treatment about the abscess that comes in marriage (boil), which is not one of those boils that swell; and if you want to know the work of iron, observe whether the abscess is acute at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Therefore, do not hurry to pierce it, but let it ripen until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a chair or small stool, and have two stools or he leans, and support his back and spread his legs apart towards the opposite side of the leg; and let his knees be spread out, and put his arms under his thighs, and bind them well with a good ligament; then draw the pus towards the right side, and bring the instrument for opening the mouth of the boil, from which its form comes later; and it is necessary that when you bring this instrument, you prick the right first hole to know the depth of the boil, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not burn the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the boil with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it must put the horn of the instrument on top, and mark the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess is opened and one handles it with a soft hand, it must be covered with a plaster of lard; and when the bowl is empty, you must put boiled linen cloth moistened in rose oil or green dry oil into the wound; and place the linen cloth from the wound to the edge of the wound and over the wound and over the plaster netted linen cloth moistened with water or vinegar which has been cooked; then heal for two days after the ointment following that, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the wound and the blister by a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or longis root and aristolochia which have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is sutured in the flesh, you should avoid iron cautery, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	From childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is first necessary for the midwife to recognize the figure of natural childbirth and the signs when she sees the woman straining downward, and desires to smell the armpit: then hasten the birth of the child; then learn that this birth is according to the natural figure, and it issues from the head and follows with a second one; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press gently on her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when he descends towards his head, it is seconded by him, and the membranes of the womb are expelled from its superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes in another way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 It sometimes happens that one falls upon their feet, or the body and the shoulders, or the hands, or it happens upon the belly, or backside, and is turned by chance on the neck, or in other bad ways; in such a case it is necessary for the help to be wise and knowledgeable about these matters, and to avoid error and deception. I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out headfirst by natural birth and the woman delivers with effort, and her vitality is weak, make her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the midwife's little spatula, as shown in the following figure:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And divide the second birth canal, and strike its claw until the water that is within the womb flows out; and grasp the woman's belly as the child descends, and if it does not descend, you must fumigate her with musk of fenugreek oil of sisamum; then make her take and vomit purge, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: this will now help the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out, you must gently push them back a little at a time; and if they cannot enter, lay the woman on the stool, and raise her feet up; then tilt the stool onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not scream during tilting; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, strike the dead child with the knife that is placed here before, extract the child, and push it back in equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 Of the birth of the child upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes upon its feet, you must push it upward; and then turn it a little at a time until it is equal; then take hold of its feet and stretch them out a little at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 It may jump up to any joints if commanded to do so, making it vomit with convulsions; if it leaps away, it is as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore it should be done gently.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 If it does not leap as we have experienced, say take musk-seed from high places, oil of roses, pitch melted, and grind them all in a mortar; put this mixture inside the woman's nature (the womb) and apply this ointment externally, then let her sit in hot water up to her ribcage; when she has softened beneath, take the myrrh colander and place it under, leaving it for an hour; then have her sit on a stool, make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose closed while lightly pressing her belly, for the child now leaps around.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the birth of the child on its genitals
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, put its hands close together (one by one); then lay it on its back, and hang its feet downwards, and let it lie on the bed; bend its hands little by little, and then grasp its hands above the belly, and break its hips bones below until it is arranged downwards; if the child does not cry, take its feet and turn them inward, then turn the belly upward, then put your hands; rock the child little by little; and order the woman to hold herself as long as the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	The birth of a child that comes out with one hand extended.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to devise a means for returning the hand: if it cannot be returned, then raise the woman and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, bend her legs outward; then bring the mustard plaster that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the stool, and try to return the hand; rock the child according to its natural figure, and make it vomit, and order her to hold herself until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Hold the baby by the neck and spread your hands apart, then turn your body towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the servant hold his hand, then twist it little by little and gently; and when it is equal, place natural muscle-relaxant of height and oil on it, as we have said, then command it to move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to take hold of it; and make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way, treat all similarly
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When farting occurs in this manner throughout the second stage, strike the caul at your fingernail until the moisture is voided; and if the child swells up on its face and neck, strike it from the buttocks so that it is not held back, and the child dies; then push the child in, as far as you must, and command the woman to take hold of herself lightly. Then it will pass easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the birth of twins   (In this context, "gemelz" refers to twins, as "gele" means a twin in Old French)
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Note that twins are born frequently and sometimes three or four; and this is not unusual, it happens often.   (The text uses Old French numerals "iii" for 3 and "iiij" for 4)
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 These are strange things that do not live unless they are named; I know they multiply and are eager for the one who conceives them, who is linked to filth; and sometimes they emerge naturally like worms under a horse, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 If they emerge noisily, the treatment should be as we have said, and the balsam shall be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do thus according to what is worth moving towards salvation.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb of a woman for one or two or three or four or five or six, or up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measure of the wise glorious one; and it is necessary that the balsam knows this, because sometimes similar things happen; do accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you cure a woman of a dead or stillborn child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to operate with your hands; then you must know if the woman is of good health, and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should lie on her back with her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the assistant touches her with both hands, or she may be tied to the bed so she is not treated in the removal of the child; then anoint the husband's mouth with oils moistened with musk and fenugreek seed and linseed; then anoint the assistant's hands with these oils and musks; then he gently thrusts into the woman, ensuring that it enters the place that is suitable; and be careful that the baby emerges from the head, otherwise it may tear in other places; and pierce the child's crown with a sharp instrument, or puncture its neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or near the navel or by the ribs, and if the removal is at the feet, then pierce or pinch and break the bones gently; and you should hold the instrument in your right hand, and place the handle between your left thumb and index finger, and thrust gently with all your hand into any of the places we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty place; and this is the shape of the instrument:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then insert opposite each other as often required, so that the extraction is even; and then make them even while moving from one side to the other, in order for them to be released, and they should be notched to hold them in place, as shown in the figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if a part remains, you can use oil and pinch one of your fingers, and push it into that part, and pull the other part; and if no part remains, place the notch or higher up, and do this until it comes out entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be returned by holding, you must roll it up in a cloth until it comes out completely; then break it at the joint of the sole or the side, and do this with the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is narrow at the birth canal, or if there is a narrow passageway assembled in the head, you must insert the pointed spatumile between your fingers, and push the head and extract the narrow passageway; or you can use the instrument called "almidach", which will help to form the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and do the same if the child has a large natural head swelling; then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the head jumps out and it cannot be held in place using forceps, it should be cut open, as much as necessary until the narrow passageway is exposed; and if it cannot be delivered, you can crush it into pieces as small as possible. If it is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, you must pierce it repeatedly until the narrow passageway appears.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the delivery is easy, and the guidance towards the mouth of the birth canal is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is protruding from the abdomen or the anus, you must push it back into place covered with a cloth over the hand; and press the abdomen or the anus, until the moisture that is there subsides; and if other members are dislocated, and the joint remains, push the ball of your hand deep into the wound, and pull it out; then push in one direction or two, and pull it further; and if the wound caused by the protrusion is contracted due to an abscess that has formed, you must not try to enlarge it, but instead provide moist and greasy substances; and provide compresses, and smear them with warm, softening, and moistening agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the child is on his side, and you can place it straight, introduce what we have said in the live child; and if there is no ability to do so, pull it out piece by piece, leaving nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done that, apply what we have said in abscesses which come in marriage; and if bleeding comes out, it should be put in hot binding, and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman whose womb had been dead, then the first doctor consulted with another on this matter and revived the fetus.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess appeared in the buttock, and swelled so much that it opened up, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned to care for it, and I thought about it for a long time, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed strong plaster on it, and a bone came out, and after some days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I want the wound and take out the bone as long as the woman is in her best position; and the woman lives for a long time in this way, and after some time a little pus comes out from the side; and I have never heard of this chapter except because when masters find a strange thing, they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the marriage to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here follows the form of the pressor, to which one applies books; and at two turnings to the two heads of the two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 The cornels (used in cautery) should be more subtle than the restrictor, and they should be made of ebony or box; and the hole in the rod should be large, and the edges of the holes, and a length of half a palm; and between the two limbs there should be two joints of the same rod, which should be tightened on one side and the other, by half a palm's length or slightly more; and these two joints are inserted into the hole of the marris to open when turning the two corns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, more slender and lighter in appearance, should be made from the rod of ebony or box, similar to pliers; and it should have two prongs, as you see, a length of one palm, and width of two fingers; and when you are ready to open the marris with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging down and legs spread open, then insert the two prongs side by side into the marris, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs; then open your hand with the entire instrument as you did with the pliers, according to the amount that you want to open the mouth of the marris, until the baby comes out as it wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These tools are all covered and have similar shapes; and when the physician has arranged them, he works more quickly, and higher for humans due to their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Never leave the tool unprepared, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold back her afterbirth, and then make her vomit with a strong emetic, and hold your hands on her mouth and nose; if she jumps due to this, it's good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If she does not do this, take the pot or basin, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the woman, such as dittany, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a cloth or lid on the pot, and the other end in the woman's mouth, and hold it until the vapors enter the woman; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second one jumps hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment and does not heal, as instructed by the midwife, she should moisten her left hand with sesame oil or mustard plaster and then apply it to nature, and wait for it to soften; and when she has found it, she should take it and stretch it little by little straight, so that the husband does not resist extraction; but it should be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come out and detach.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the husband's private parts have been stretched out, we have said the cure for dilatation and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not heal with what has been said, ensure you do not pull too hard; but it is necessary that he who is at the husband's private parts ties him to the woman's leg, then anoint it with ointment four-formula; if she can, she will close it and it will heal; however, when she can, a bad smell comes to the stomach and head of the patient, and it injures her.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary to use suitable fumigations for this: no one has proven fumigations of dill and dried figs effective.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for the retention of flowers and the second birth is as follows:    (This sentence is incomplete, so I couldn't provide a full translation)
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it appears to be like a glass container, and the soft part is placed inside its nature, and the shoulders are held wide open over the fire; and let there be fumigation over the coals, and the tinder until it is ruined, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to drill the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born without a foundation pierced, but rather stopped up by some subtle plaster: therefore the ball should be perforated with that plaster to its proper depth, and not with a sharp spur; and ensure that it does not touch the wound; then put damp linen in wine and oil, and apply ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will reopen, place a leaden cannula over it (the boil), and leave it for several days, and remove it when the pus begins to move towards the rooms (of the body).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this sudden swelling of wound or abscess occurs; it should be covered: whether it is healed, as we have said in the treatment of a poultice.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodules and grow larger if they come from above the foundation or in the space between two parts, whether there is one fistula or more; and when that nodule becomes old, it should be operated on, and moisture wakes up a blister or thin boil, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by those who see or experience discharge or ventosity, when the patient experiences discharge, and possibly urination.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach up to the bladder and halfway down the penis; they reach up to the joint of the thigh, and up to the knee joint.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus it is recognized the fistula persistent at the base, not persistently; and it is that you bite your finger or the base, and bite a thin needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twist in it.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 If it has a twist, then you bite a fine splint or horsehair until you feel the splint or hair on your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no pus or wind or worm comes out of it as we have said: know that it does not perforate; hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has perforated up to the bladder or up to the conduit of urine, if it spouts urine and cannot heal with medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated up to the joint of the leg, then the splint comes to the level; if there is no twist and the pain around it subsides, then it is that it should always be bowed, and no medicine or treatment with ointment is of any use for it; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of foolish men who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In one who is not paralyzed and is not old, with hope of healing by means of iron, as I have experienced, the patient lies between your hands on their back; you raise their legs up to their thighs, and bend their thighs towards their stomach; then thrust a tent of iron or wood, if there is any curvature, until you know where the curvature comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels pain around the foundation, then you must thrust your index finger there, and if it gives way then the curvature has been pierced; if it is covered or you feel a hard spot there, then know that it is paralyzed; do not try to move it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 One should always say that some can be cured well, but it happens rarely; and the aid that one does, is when one heats the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as before said; and put it very hot in the fistula, until it comes out from the base; and do this twice or three times, until you know that these charred substances are burnt, which resemble a feather of an eye; and then cure with moistened tents in butter, until the char is gone, then cure with ointment soothing and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed otherwise and the fistula is pierced up to the base and between the finger and the fistula a thick cover of charcoal or syfac is placed, and you see the fistula through the cover with care; if the cautery is applied from the beginning of the fistula, and pushed forward towards the fistula, and then the cautery after, until it reaches the top of the fistula; then the fistula will be freed, and charred; then separate those charred substances that resemble a feather of an eye, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound gapes and separates, cut between you and it, then cauterize with fire or medicine ointment.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The fire cautery brings about two good things: the burning of these adjacent charred areas, and the extinguishing of blood and drying of moisture; then it cures tents moistened with butter or cooked cheese until the flesh turns brown, and the charred areas are buried in the boil; then it heals the wound with ointments made from hard char and dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it becomes healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	If a fistula comes all the way up to the bottom, and is separated from the body, push your thumb or finger against the bottom, and check it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the boil and between it is the fabric or leather or charred areas close to piercing, there should be no recourse but the path of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you strike to the bottom, or if possible apply tents and heal as before; do not go too deep, so that you do not cover the foundation and bring on suppuration through willful action; then heal, as we have said; perhaps it may become healthy again, or you remove that covering and clean where it was pierced, either with a tent or another tool provided; then burn away the charred material in the wound, as much as possible; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula at the distant part from the foundation: it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes abscesses are formed in this manner: and when you squeeze the tent (possibly a pimple) into the abscess, it is where the base of the tent adjoins the skin above, take a lance with a sharp point according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and insert one thread twisted in two, and press the tent on the entire length of the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head (or top).
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is pus (pus-filled) on the edge of the base inside, then draw out the thread of that tent using your finger or base; pull out the head of the thread, bring the two heads together, and press them against each other, and leave for a day or two without moving it; hold it once when the threads touch those hard spots (pus-heads) that are between them, and open the abscess; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce through, make it pierce in all possible ways, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is not advisable to treat a dislocated joint by covering it tightly and then curing it while it is still unhealthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spur-like spine from which a fistula is made is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other; not so, because one should not strike what one should not strike, as you see here:
des emorroydes	piles (hemorrhoids)
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 The emorydes (cysts) come in two ways: either they are within the foundation, like a piece of resin, with small and large ones, and on the outside there is blood, and one or more of them; and they protrude from the foundation and at its base; but those that protrude have some moisture, and sometimes there is a little liquid citron juice or blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure for these that are within the foundation is to command the patient to strain in order to evacuate them through his chambers, until the foundations come out, and then the threads can be seen; if you hurry, pinch it with pliers or hold it with your nail, then strike its roots; and if the threads cannot hold because of moisture, take a piece of linen, cloth, or cotton; and bind them to your fingers, then strike, and sprinkle some hot powders on top that act like cautery, or cauterize them as described in the chapter of cautery, until they heal completely; if the foundations cannot come out, you should enema the patient with a harsh, biting enema to clean what is around the foundation, so it can come out openly; when the patient strains and the threads are outside the foundation, the cure is easy; it is that you take hold of them with your nail or pliers, strike them, and treat as we have said, until they heal, and fear the incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You must apply the stitching in this manner: take twisted thread and insert it into a needle, then pull the thread above and pierce the needle from another side, twist both ends of the thread beneath the needle, if necessary; make a knot with the thread, then tighten the thread, remove the needle, and do the same with all the others. Leave some space for bleeding; place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the wound foundation and tell the patient to rest. Then leave it until it scabs over, when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other remedies, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The dry heat of the fire or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often, there is dryness from fever in the intestines, and due to the natural constraint, when the sickness is old and medicine has no effect.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you cauterize the tip of a spatula or your nail with the skin above it, so it does not get moist; then let it heal as needed; and if it cannot heal, then repeat the shaving more forcefully than before until it heals and is skinned; then let it heal again.
dou fremit	toothache
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A blister is a small growth found near the body and grows quickly; sometimes it is mistaken for frostbite, causing death-like shivering throughout the body, spreading to all parts, especially the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is that you take a wire of an ostrich feather or a strong chicken feather and place the wire around the frostbite, making circles around it; then turn your hand around the entire wire until it covers the frostbite completely and makes it boil; then burn the frostbite from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do as with a cat's incision of honey or iron according to this form, and be subtle beneath and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, to keep the tooth, and press more; And if you see, cauterize the froth, as it is in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster   (enema)
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make an enema of silver or arsenic, or melted beeswax or mallet; and sometimes they make these small and large instruments according to those for whom they are prepared.  (For the treatment of different ailments)
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when treating children who are weak and painful, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the cucurbit is both small and large, or the belly is tied in this manner:   (Note that "cucurbit" was incorrectly provided instead of "clistere".)
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And it should have an opening where the abdomen is sewn, as you see, and the shoulders should be pierced within; and on one side there should be two holes, and in the other one; and let the abdomen or the belly be filled with a bladder of an animal or parchment, and pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be a space; then insert strong thread through the holes, either silk or linen in X or Y shape around, and gather the belly like a she-goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or goose fat, or similar thing, then insert it gently; then spread the administrators with their two hands together until it is all visible, then remove the clyster, and tie the patient's legs to the parity, and if the medicine appears, press as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you plaster the patient with belly distention caused by gas, and the medicine appears to work quickly, continue until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoids are foundation or abscess, whether it be the suppository also as for a child; and this is the shape of the subtle suppository on which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	in the treatment of wounds;
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment for wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments and medicines for hands, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by the thrust of a sword, cut of a knife and scissors, or lance or fist or arrow, or similar things; or those made according to the body's laws, such as wounds on the neck, head, side, belly, liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound or sore comes about, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is due to piercing or similar things, and the skin is all torn and the wound is large; doubt the presence of an abscess high: make it drain from the head itself, even if blood comes out from the wound, and let it drain in the opposite direction of the damaged part; and have the patient avoid filling himself with wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it does not drain, reduce the meat, do not drink wine, nor eat fatty foods; and place on the wound, if an abscess comes up there, soft cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no abscess, place on the fresh wound, with all its blood, if it is not moving due to air, a powder that I will say a little later; and if the fire has moved it, place some ointments on until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by sutures, bring them together by sewing, as I shall say for the abdominal wounds, with suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed by bone, open and only stays together with a little bit, press it; then heal the wound with medicine, replace hard flesh instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as cooked heads (testes) and cooked wheat, also like pulses (peas), etc.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find or skin decay, not adhering to the bone, press it all down and pour boiling water on it, then heal it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein without a clot, which cannot stop bleeding with medicines, tie the artery and if it becomes dislocated, hold it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if the wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy: it is that you put this powder on which hardens as soon as the arrows have moved [the wound].
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the way of the powder is: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; three parts of live coal, and grind it finely, then apply to the wound and press firmly until it purges well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well and leave it to heal, if it does not swell; for medicine is not removed while it is still healing.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes they do this with only chalk, when there is no incense nor dragon's blood, but the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the fire has opened the wound, by all means do not put this powder on it; but apply some digestive ointments or flour of barley made with water and honey until it boils; then heal it with other remedies until it heals.
