Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound    (literal translation)
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one in the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.   (literal translation)
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerves, there is no other device but to let them heal naturally and not put anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, as the substance of nerves is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as water boiled in gentle heat, and mixed with rose oil, and boiled again in mild heat, and other stones of this kind, and moist immediately afterwards.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, bind it with strips, then let it heal until it becomes healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 If the wounds are deep and filled with pus, pierce or open them lower down; if the arteries are cut, bleeding will come out, so cauterize it, and lance and cauterize as needed; if the spine of the throat is cut or the glands, keep the flesh from touching the throat but place it in its natural position, then hold it in place for a while, and treat with decayed ointments until it heals; if the wound presses against the bone, open it up; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and leave those that you cannot have until the wound suppurates and discharges pus; if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on it as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is bone in the wound and a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or sword wound, and the wound is deep, look to see if the patient shows signs of breathlessness from the wound: know then that the wound is fatal; and if the wound is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it immediately, nor bind it for the blood that would cause it to dissolve quickly and return to the heart, and let the patient die; but apply attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 or 4 days, or more; and there will be no spasms, nor bad tremors of heart or signs of breathlessness from the wound; and when you see good condition, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat the wound and other treatments while it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, then open it up, knowing that there is a fistula; treat it as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is from a sword or knife and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it accordingly; if it is large, sew it; if it is small, apply powder; and if it has penetrated the bone and taken pieces with it, either clean the wound and pull out the pieces; and if they cannot be pulled out, let the wound drain, and align the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the decision is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The displacement of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The dislocation of the abdomen is large, medium and small; from a large wound, the intestines sometimes escape once or the intestine's nerves, through which they are incised; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because the intestines have to be put back in place with difficulty, unless they are put back piece by piece; because the intestines swell suddenly when they feel the cold, they shrink more easily, and therefore the medium-sized wound is better, because the intestines are reset in their place more easily than for others. And know that the wound of the abdomen is according to four ways: the two common sutures occur in the abdominal wound, and the sutures of other body wounds and two other specific ones are common for other wounds; but they are more appropriate with the suture of the abdomen, and I will say one and explain it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the internal organs protrudes out of it, and there is little to repair, this is easy in one of the two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in any manner: moisten a sponge or dampen a thin cloth only with hot water, or cook it in hot squill and cyperus root and spike, and massage the intestines until the swelling disappears; and sometimes do this with wine restraining, and it is necessary to have it so that it can be drained.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling separate, anoint the intestine with hot or cold water and rotten vegetables, because this closes the entrance to very little; and if it cannot enter, make a small wound with the instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to drain it, that we should not cut it without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: slice it open inside but do not tear it apart, and look at its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines fall out, you should put them back in their natural place in their proper position, if you have the ability, because it is important to do so.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the part below the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; if it is in the part below the navel, then raise the head and feet higher than the parts below; similarly, if the wound is in one of the two sections of the belly, you should take care that the damaged section is raised above the other; and in this way, you should administer what I say for large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 Place small wounds with what suits you, then have a compassionate person who dyes all the wound's edges with his hand, and gather the lips; and this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you take one or more needles, according to the size of the wound's width, then leave space from the chief of the wound, and sew a needle where it has good strong thread; and pierce the two skins with the two skins beneath, which is under the skin, until you make it pierced from that part, and gather the two chiefs of the skin together threefold; then bind a double thread around the needle in two parts, then assemble the two skins of the wound accordingly, then leave space, and sew another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what is necessary with the needles, until the entire wound is bound; and the needles should be moderate, neither too thin nor too thick, for thin needles pierce all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be moderate. And it is not good to push the needles too far from the flesh and skin, so that they do not injure or open the wound before suturing; then sew the heads of the needles, so that they do not poke the patient while sleeping, and put weights or bandages on the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires one needle or two needles for second stitching, and it is that you assemble the two skins of the skin and the two skins beneath together with one needle where it has medium strong thread; and when you have sewn all the parts threefold, then withdraw the needle to the part where you started, in the manner of sewing cloth; and place space between each stitch the thickness of a minor egg; this suturing is called human, and I sewed a wound with a man who had a belly, which was pierced by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and it was the intestines two palms wide, and the wound was within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestine before it had been XXIV hours [outside], and the wound was sewn up for 15 days, and it healed, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And they had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with liniment, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicine; and I put sense more on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Furthermore, I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the skin directly, if the chief [layer] of the flesh or that which you have pierced with the needle, pierce it again from the other side of the inner part to the outer; and the meaning of this suturing is that you sew as a pelter does fur, and leave one time the flesh of one part, and take it again of the other, until the suture is completely accomplished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of stitching, as Galen describes it, is done by joining the two parts together naturally, and applying one edge of the mirror to the other edge, in this manner: stick a needle or edge of the mirror close by, and pierce only that place; leave the two edges of the mirror aside; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner, through the two edges of the mirror; then pierce both again from the outer part to the inner, in the two other edges of the mirror on the opposite side; and this is the more common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens said this word and it is confirmed by others, that the belly should be sewn with two needles, each having thread in them; and one needle should be driven in from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when the wound is within the belly, the stitching is more difficult than other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is similar to that of other wounds: it is that when you discover the fresh wound full of blood, before the arrow has moved it, you should replace the intestine and the flesh; then put powder healing char on it, and if the arrow has moved it, apply any available ointment until the wound stops bleeding; stitch the skin, sew the sifac, and the mirach; then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put old cotton on it, as soon as it begins to stop bleeding, two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 Since the wounds are simple in many cases and if you doubt that the wound spreads to the main limbs, it is necessary to moisten light linen with warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the swelling, and under the saddle; and if there is pain or rotting in the belly and this happens frequently, clisterize with black wine, especially if the rotting comes up to the intestines; and pierce it and know that when it is the large intestines, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine known as "jeun" cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is because of the inflammation of the veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the gristle jumps out of the wound, put it back as you would an intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned yellow or black, you must cut away the black part, so that blood does not come from it, because there are veins and arteries; then seize what is between the ligament, and hang the two heads suspended from the area below the wound to facilitate extraction when the gristle falls out, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the eyeball
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 If the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I have seen that a man was wounded or pierced by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became abscessed and developed into a fistula, with discharge and flatulence; I cured it according to what I knew, and did not stop treating it until it healed, and the edges sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it sealed, I doubted that the patient had an illness in his stomach; and there was no illness, but he improved with better nutrition, and eatings and drinkings; and any experimentors said that when a small wound is in the intestine, it should be sewn up in this manner: take large clamps, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the clamp has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches the mouth open; and then hit the head, and hold it so it cannot unfasten, then put another clamp after in the same manner until the wound is fully captured; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head of the intestine becomes inflamed, no harm comes to the patient, and the intestine can be tied with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of the thread of the animal's intestine which is sharpened, then tie it to the head of the thread made of flax twine, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine and mend it in the wound; and this method of stitching does not provide anything but hope and faith; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no remedy or health, except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it heals and forms a cavity, is universally called "fistula", and the same when it is closed and becomes hollow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And fistula is according to the truth, a knot filled with hard and white matter, where there is no pain, and is as hollow as the feather of an eggshell; sometimes clear and hollow, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times quite large; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed and has no flesh, it is not a wonder if it is due to one of the nine causes: namely, by the small amount of blood or flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and above the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or it has too much pus; or the place is destroyed, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or the corruption is the nature of pestilence; or because the region has a slow digestion, and healing is late and weak by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the medicines for their cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it is necessary that I tell you the treatment for fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or the intestine, or the bladder, or one of the sides, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and it is such that affects the property of the principal member, and similar areas.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all such fistulas are difficult to heal, except for labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come as I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it recognized, take a tent of fat or metal, if the fistula is straight, pierce it; and if the fistula is crooked, seek a thin probe of wood, for probes bend with curvature; and if the fistula has been torn and you cannot seek it well by probes, cleanse it through one of the openings, for moisture flows from one opening to another, and cleanses; then heal it as well as you can, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and whether it is closed completely, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when pressed by your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know where it is, and whether it is far from jointure, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the areas that I have said, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the rotten flesh and corrupted parts that are inside; and then heal until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply rooted straightly, you must cut completely, as much as possible, then put moistened medicine-filled probes into it, and push them to the top of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains in the depth; and then put salve on fresh char, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve does not bother or major limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove all the corruption as much as possible, then treat with charms appropriate for healing until it heals; and if it does not heal and returns bowed, know that you are not yet done: strip and clean as deep as you can, remove all the corruption, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep that you cannot reach it, know that there is no other means but to wait for nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can extract with pliers, remove it with the appropriate tool for that purpose, and if there are many bones, remove all of them without leaving any; and if moisture opposes you or there is error or fear, strike the moisture and the source of corruption with a hammer and charcoal, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something irritating pus on the wound and leave it until the flesh surrounds the bone, and then the bones will be easier to move; and if it is a large bone, as in the leg or thigh, press only the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of corruption that reaches the bone molecule, it must be cut off and covered up to the corruption, and then heal until it heals; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg due to something coming from within the body, and pus accumulated in the leg, and it did not have a way to escape; but they foolishly worked on it until the abscesses opened, and much pus came out, and it became a fistula, and many people who were bowed and weak with moisture of the body gathered around him; and many tried to cure him for two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines they used to treat him, and the corruption that came out through the wounds at great expense; and the young man's body became red, and he had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I inserted a tent in one of the wounds, and then I searched for all the wounds, and found that some came towards each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 Then I hurried and cut in one of the wounds as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone within; I considered that only this bone was corrupted, except for what I left behind; and I began to heal the wound with salves for a long time, but could not close it; then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found continuous corruption in the bone, and left it, and then closed it up, and thought of healing the limb; but I could not go any further than cutting around one palm's breadth of the bone, and let it hang loose, then I healed it with salves; and it became healthy and closed quickly, but it was no longer necessary to continue the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation (procedure), it often bleeds profusely, but it became completely healthy, and a hard cyst grew in the bone's place, and it was well-positioned and had no harm or disadvantage in any way, neither in its appearance nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 If the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a suture, and tie it at the open end of the bone, and command someone to pull it up; place another thicker linen suture over the cyst that is below the bone, and tighten it so that you draw the corrupt cyst downwards, and expose the healthy cyst in the place where you want it to be, ensuring it does not harm the healthy cyst; place fire or a plaster under the bone to melt the corrupt cyst; stay like this as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and should also be done again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 If the bone is rotten and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, you should remove all the flesh first; then place charcoal under it, and then press from one side to another on the area of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at a joint, strike the dislocated joint, and hold the bone that contains the other part; and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no other choice but to cut it; and if the corruption is at the end of the hand or foot, this is very difficult, but you must examine the corruption and see how it can be opened; clean it in every way that you can, but make sure not to harm the vein or nerve; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the type of bone and its appearance, its thickness and its subtlety, its size and its smallness, and its hardness; and therefore, you should prepare an instrument suitable for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the diseases; and choose the tool that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulder may dislocate either internally or externally; and when you have tried the remedy for this corruption through medication and it does not work, it is necessary to cover that member up to the level where the corruption occurs, so that the patient may escape death from this, or a greater evil, namely the defect of the member; and the signs are that the limb becomes black as if it were burned by fire, and later turns black, for the corruption of the member spreads from one to another and affects the entire body; hasten with the covering, and if it is due to the attack of certain venomous animals, such as sea scorpions, snakes, and similar, cover the head when the corruption is in the throat, and do not give it any space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches as far as the hand, strike at the joint so that the corruption does not reach to the arm; and if it reaches the arm, strike at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no remedy can be found other than the amount of its potency; and thus one should act when the corruption comes or stops: if it comes at the first joint, strike after the next joint; and if it comes or stops, strike the whole affected area; and if it moves to the leg, strike at the knee joint; and if it goes beyond the knee, there is no other remedy for the sick but to let them die; and the manner of striking or soothing the member is that you bind it above and below, extend one of the strips downward, and another strip upward, and you loosen the flesh that is between the two strips with a spatula wide enough so that the bone is exposed; then strike or soothe, and place linen cloth on each side so that the soothing does not touch the healthy tissue, and bring another injury and abscess to the sick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some powders that restrain; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my presence: he had a blackness which seemed to be burned by fire, and this corruption first appeared in his foot under the heel, so that it consumed the entire heel; and when the man saw the corruption, he hastily covered the heel with something, and it healed; and a long time later, the corruption returned to the heel or the hand, and it came to me, and I gave him remedies after the purification of his body, but the corruption could not be stopped; and he asked that I amputate his hand, and I did not want, for I had hope of restoring the matter; and also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, as his vitality was weak; and he gave up all hope, returned to his earth, and hastily covered his hand with something, and it healed; and I have told this story only for this reason: that one does otherwise, if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Aposteme sometimes occurs in the charnut place and stays for such a long time that it causes a large abscess of pus; and then it breaks open, and the pus jumps out, and the place remains open as a wound, like a warrior's; and the skin which is above it is as thin as unbleached linen, and does not go all the way to the bone or nerve. Such a disease is called "sain", but not "fistule"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone entirely, it is called "fistule". The skin should be cut around it completely, just as one would cut linen; and it will not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the skin hardens and the corruption is not yet complete, and the skin thickens with flesh, cure it with a clistere thus: check if the breast is large and the area around it smells bad; then apply an Egyptian-made medicine clistere: take asafetida, oil, litharge, equally, and cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take as needed from this, make it watery and honey, and apply the clistere to the breast, and hold the anus; leave the medicine for two hours, then remove it straining; do this often, until the breast is softened and the pus is expelled; and at no time clisterize with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes from a vine stick, pour water on it, then strain, and apply, until you know that the breast is well purified; and if the patient cannot endure this, or the Egyptian medicine and the water of ashes, then clisterize with water and honey or mead where the mead has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes the blood thicken; and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well purified, then apply whatever heals the sores in the breast, and take emplastrum diaphoretic, and make it with rose oil and vine; or clisterize with various medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken their properties or treatments for ointments; and if the opening in the breast is small, and the clistere applicator cannot enter, enlarge it slightly with a knife, and apply an Egyptian-made linen, or basilicon ointment, until it is sufficiently enlarged; and if the wound is too large, leave it open only enough for the clistere to enter, and if the pus from the breast protrudes above, cover or place lower than that.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	1. When the bone is fully fractured, do not allow any char to enter it; and if you cannot cover the wound beneath as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bone moves to its lowest point because when the bone is fully fractured, do not allow any char to enter it and if you cannot cover the wound beneath as you see fit, arrange it in this manner: the bone should move gently downwards, but do not leave anything of the bone; take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and place a linen cloth over the entire wound; then press forcefully towards the pierced wound, which is larger than the first, because afterwards bind it tightly with another cloth according to the size of the pierced wound, and place it on the pierced wound to align the bone, but do not remove the large cloth until after several days; and the one who is on the pierced wound should frequently remove it in order to realign the bone, and be aware of what comes out from the bone, whether it is poison or pus or something indigestible; also pay attention if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that rises on the pierced wound, know that the wounds have already healed, and approach health; then release it in the morning, or the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the liniment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	If the breasts overflow with undigested matter for many days, know that the breasts do not swell.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle venomous worms come after a long time, do not despair of health, for it approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And there are those whose flesh takes a long time to heal in their wounds, and of those who act contrary to this; and if the breast swells indigestibly after many days, know that it will not heal; and if the breast does not heal after being drained, and is swollen, apply drying medicines with dry substance and wet virtue, such as oil of roses, and equal parts of old wine in substance; then mix and use them; and the same can be done more effectively when oil of roses is unavailable, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, powder them on the honey while it is over the fire, and then apply the dough to the breast, and sometimes an astrologer long is administered, and roots of celestial plants, which are like flour and centaur; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make powder, and put on the honey I said before, and use it; and if the patient is not healed by this cure, know that corruption is complete, and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or ligaments; if the patient is not healed by this cure, then know that the corruption is complete, and make an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or ligaments; if the patient is not healed by this cure, then heal with a fistula cure as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail bed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Parasitic abscess originates beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or sometimes in other parts; and when it grows, and care is not taken, the abscess spreads, runs and spills pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly the entire nail; then the corrosion reaches the bone, causing a strong-smelling pain, and the joint becomes wide and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, and cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great aid if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail grows into the flesh, begins to swell, and bleeds, you must put heat underneath the nail so as not to burn the flesh, and push it upwards, and gently and lightly strike the nail with a sharp instrument to remove it; then heal it with ointments until it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and draw pus out, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see it becoming corrupted, strike it with a splinter as before mentioned, then let it heal until it is healthy; and if it is wounded and hurts greatly, it must be healed first; then strike the nail with a sharp instrument in a crosswise cutting, but watch that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the hand gradually subsides.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 One must straighten the fingers that are born in some people by chance, and they are all flesh, and sometimes there is skin or bone there, and occasionally there is a nail; and none of these grow from the root of a joint, or their growth is in one of our palms.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one that is born in any nail of the hand does not grow, and the one that is born at the joint of the hand, by chance sometimes grows; the shape of the one that is flesh is light, in this manner: cut it back to its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure, take care.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who is born or should be in the last nail, you must cut the flesh roundly up to the bone first, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and then treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together in the fingers also come together by birth, or by injury, or by fire burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If it is necessary to sew up that wound, the limbs should be repaired according to their natural forms; then put between two cloths or linen moistened in oil of roses, so they do not stick together; or you can put between two thin pieces of wood until the limbs are joined as needed.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Similarly, if it comes to either of its sides with the palm, you strike the joint as necessary.
des vils	 of peasants
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 These are veins that are thick and full of melancholic superfluidities, which come in many members of the body; and it happens more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purge of bile at times, and then the healthy from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The iron cure is according to two methods: one is when they are sewn and the black blood is drawn out; and the other method is that you tie the vein and let it all drain out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The size should be as follows: first stretch the leg with hot strong water until the flesh becomes soft, then hold the patient's leg above the knee up to the part below the groin; then cut open the vein in I or II or III, of a large size, then separate and draw out black blood up to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the disease can withstand; and then tie it, and command him to bandage himself with meat broth colored black; and start the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and this helps the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The bandaging should be as follows: lay the patient's leg flat if there is much hair on it, then immerse it in water or put it in a bath and stretch the patient's leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins; if you don't have water, heat the leg with fire, and then cut open the vein at the long part of the thigh to the top of the knee or below to the ankle; tear the skin around the vein from both sides, exposing it when it is felt; it should appear red and black, and where the skin surrounds the vein seems like a white cord; then push the meat down, allowing it to swell under the skin, and then gently tie it at the ankle, then cut another opening 3 inches further; tear the skin over the vein again from both sides, exposing it, then draw it out as you have done, and move to another incision; then make another cut, or more if needed, then draw it out, and tie it to the second knot, as you did before; then make another cut, or more as necessary, draw it out, and tie it at the end of the bone; then pull and draw out until it is completely emptied, then bind it; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, insert a sharp thin double-threaded needle, bind and pull, and push it down under the meat; turn your hand from side to side until it is emptied; be careful not to cut it, for if it cuts, you cannot draw it out or lift it, which would harm the patient; and when you have treated it all, place linen soaked in wine and oil over the wound; and cure it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the eye is contracted, twisted and rolled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it open but do not cover it; pull it out as we have stated before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The form of the iron used to pierce the eye should be curved and not break, but should not pierce the vein; it is of large curvature, for if it were thin, it would pierce the vein. However, it should be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is embedded in the legs, in warm areas where no grass or trees grow, and in dry land without moisture; it can also grow elsewhere, and this happens due to a swelling that comes from beneath the skin, as it grows within the body like a snake, embedding itself between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg and then the joint changes and the vein starts to forcefully appear, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the joint opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of wood from 7 to 10 inches long and sew it, and leave the wood on the leg, and each time it swells outwards, you wrap it around the wood again and sew; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the rest, but do not cover its root until it is completely out; for if you cover it, it returns to the flesh, causing abscess and pus or poor health; therefore, it should be treated carefully until the head, and nothing remains on the body; and this vein is sometimes when it is treated 5 or 10 fingers long, or even a foot. Once I had a case where it was 10 fingers long, and when you cauterize it, you press the iron or the hot iron, and pierce until it all comes out; empty the matter that is inside, and apply external pus-reducing medicines for several days, then cure as you would with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes in opening this vein, the hand slips, especially when it is open at the joint of the foot or finger; much blood spills out and it jumps back; so you must heal it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land because it often appears in cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes through the entire body expanding and contracting, and feels from one member to another until it reaches the skin or bursts out; and it is infected with corruption of certain humors, as snakes, serpents, roundworms, or ascaris in the stomach; and there is doubt about its harmfulness, for when it goes through the body, it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, possibly enters it, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to be treated and drained, one can force it out only when it moves: therefore, you must bind the limb above and below with a strong rope tightly, then strike upon it and pull it out, and if it goes in deeply into the flesh and cannot be seen, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it runs oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold a lizard-like clamp under it, then strike upon it and pull it out; and one must use the patient with purification of body medicines soluble for bad humors, and avoid consuming foul-smelling foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 Of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our land "wind-affliction", and it is a pain that moves in some members, and spreads from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and I found her arm swollen, and I saw a small boil in the armpit of the arm; then afterwards, it rose up like a worm towards the shoulder, faster than anything alive, like a live knife when it cuts from one thing to another; the pain spread from that place, and entered the shoulder, and then shortly after ran throughout the body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she turned around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from one member to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 In addition, I would have wished many who wanted to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it for myself, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and due to this, such constrained windiness appeared; and it does not apply according to this reasoning to those who are delicate and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you wish to cure this disease and the patient feels such pain, if it opens as we have said, lie it above and below quickly, then strike above so that the constrained windiness goes to another place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, cure it with such things that expel windiness, like fetid pills, pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	 arrows
