Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their shapes and according to the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, small ones, sharp, and blunt; and those with two edges, and those with tongues, and those with segments; and the one that falls into any member falls according to two ways: either in a principal member, like the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, kidneys, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it falls into any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appears: then it is necessary that you take care of extracting this arrow, because death comes in many forms; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not completely embedded, pull it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and a swelling appears on top of the skull, is when scotomie (blindness), scole (hardness), esvertin (convulsion), roujor (redness), and inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, vomiting of bile; and possibly without fever from the nose or ears; and possibly losing speech and voice; and a white, moist discharge comes from the wound, resembling pus, and in addition it swells like bruise of flesh; and if this sign appears, avoid treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 And the sign of an arrow when it strikes or pierces the liver, is that it lies near the left kidney and feels like it has been inserted into a hard object, not empty; possibly the liver becomes swollen as if with pus, and black blood flows from the wound, and coldness and cold sweat comes, and fainting: then there is no doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that never pierces the flesh is when bubbles rise from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, sighs loudly and seeks fresh air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if an arrow falls into the mattress of the bed, it is removed between the ribs; and it causes great pain, deep breathing, and groaning; and all the limbs of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If an arrow falls into the stomach, possibly something from indigested meat may escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If an arrow falls into the belly and nothing escapes from the intestines through the wound, there is no hope in the treatment or removal of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, as the hand, arm, throat, shoulder, armpit, backbone, waist, hips, legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of this you do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to the man that an arrow or shard struck the root of his nose; I pulled it out from another side below the ear fat, and it came out without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And by playing, an arrow was retrieved that had struck the oil bag under the paper, and the arrowhead was hidden, and it could not be reached but the tip towards the trunk; and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, with a light iron tip on ears; the game was without pain, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And retrieved an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with iron ears; I had to beards, and made it thin enough that I pulled it out, and the Christian was without pain.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And I removed an arrow from the man who was either head or belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow and drew it out, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if an arrow strikes a man either in the head or back, and the wound is sewn up over it; the arrow remains inside him, and his natural condition does not change, nor does any harm occur in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And visit another man who was struck by an arrow in his face, and the wound was sewn up; he endured great pain for a long time, and many similar symptoms occurred.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And remove an arrow from the body of the prince's king, who was lying within the snow, and was slightly slanting to the right side; and the arrow was fully imbedded. I was called for his treatment after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 Found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I pierced it with a fine probe and felt nothing; but he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the arrow tip. I placed a soothing and digestive plaster on the spot as the flesh did not swell; and the arrowhead appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I left the plaster for many days, healed the wound completely, and kept him in that state for a long time until he felt the arrow within his belly; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I apply a corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it is opened, and then I probe it, and feel the head of the arrow which adheres in place; afterwards I treat the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appears visible; and it heals well within four months, and then I release the wound that I had closed with pliers, and pull it apart from both sides, and it could not come out; therefore I did not stop trying and inventing ways to extract the instrument, until I made the pliers properly, as described at the end of this chapter, until I draw it, and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the men judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored; I will then restore it, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so take care in this which I do not specify, because books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters understand well a little thing and the present and failing case, discover new work, and find a new instrument, for the things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows enter the members where they are driven only through two ways: either through the way they enter or from another side; and that which leaps out through the place where it enters is an arrow entering into flesh, and leaps out sometimes at once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, leave it until the charms are spread around, and align the joint; and in the same way, if it is pierced into the bone, and cannot come out, leave it for some days, and move it every day; then it will jump, and if it still does not jump, perforate around with a sharp instrument, until the sides are widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is pierced into the skull bone and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, or any of the accidents that I have mentioned before happen to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it is aligned after some days; for if the arrow reaches so far, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow has not been lodged deep into the bone but only slightly, and the patient experiences no severe incident and remains for some days, you should devise a means to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply inserted and cannot be removed, administer poultices around it, as I told you before; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is lodged deep inside the body and cannot be seen, you should search for it diligently; if you find it, draw it out with any suitable instrument; if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves or veins, widen the wound as much as possible; draw the arrow out when you can, and if it has ears like they hold onto something, remove the flesh that is lodged in it by half on both sides as much as you can, then bend or break the ears of the arrow to facilitate its removal; be careful not to break the arrow as this would make it harder to draw.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot pull it out in one go, push the linen cloth around it until it is reached the joints, then pull it gently, as the extraction should be done carefully.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flowing of blood hinders (the process), bring forth what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and beware of incision on the nerve and the vein, and provide means to draw out the arrowhead gently, quickly or firmly, as circumstances require; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot do so, place him according to what the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another place, opening something or the skin is swollen in one place as can be seen or felt; cut (it) then, until tongs can grasp it, and pull it out. If it jumps away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it still and then continue the extraction until it comes forth; and if it was of an arrow, push it all in; and if it fell, and you see that you must administer a forceps, use a forceps so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the forceps; and then push further, and if the arrow is caught by the forceps, push in the forceps with the pointed end entering, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is touched (by the forceps), it is necessary that you cut around where the venom is, as much as possible, then treat the wound as required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if an arrow falls or pierces the abdomen, bladder, ribs or side, and it is close enough to reach, cover it if you can; avoid covering the vein and nerve, then pull it out, then cut the wound if necessary; and cure it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to extract arrows resemble an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the hair root is similar to the feather of a bird, to guide the point of an arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pointing and straightening is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	incisions of the body common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The veins from which one recovers are thirty-one, so it has eighteen branches, that is to say: two bandages after the ears, called the "dou herbech"; and the two arteries in the two temples visible; and the two veins in the eyes' hollows, called "aspir"; and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the neck; and the two tendons that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips, which are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly healed in every arm are V: one is the cephalic, which is located on the left costal side, and it's called by the lay people "arm vein"; the median is called "fistula", composed of the cephalic and basilic, and it's called by the lay people "heart vein"; the basilic is located on the right costal side, and it's called by the lay people "abdominal vein", and it's above the elbow, and it's the one that is opened which clearly appears near the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 The cubital vein is the one that is between the ulnar and little finger, and has two rainfall systems; in the leg there are three veins: one is under the wrist on the left costal side, another subsaphenous vein at the right ankle, and the vein called "nasse", which is located at the other ankle's wrist; in the other leg, there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The first sore after the ears helps with ancient catharras and migration; and the quality of the cure, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head, rub the place or the sores with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw until the two sores appear behind the ears in the two places depending on the head; then press down on it when you feel the pulse beneath your hand, and hold firmly; then take the lancet, and thrust it through the sore up to the bone, then pull your hand all along the sore, and strike and the skin and the sore well two times through; and make the blood come out until you see; then strain and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The first vein of the two that are in the temples, is suitable for treating old, sore, and commonly occurring inflammations of the eyes; and the quality of this vein is as I say: and it is that the patient extends their neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and you feel a pulse under your chin, then press on it; then lift the skin above the vein to your chin mark, and push the lancet into it, and lift the vein up, and break it, as you have done in the other veins, and draw blood according to your need; then release the patient, and place your chin on the vein for an hour, then cover it with cotton; and then form a bandage around it and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about its treatment and its extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The vein in the forehead is as important as the cephalic vein in ancient facial diseases, and it has migrated and reddened; and the qualities are such that the patient stretches his neck while turning, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Place the tip on the vein and press from your hand or something else, allowing the blood to flow according to the quantity you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is healthy and not once during any of its workings should one use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp; and pierce through obliquely because the bone is close, and accidents may occur if the flames are too fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The veins in the two eyelids aid in redness, tearing, reddening, swelling, and facial diseases; and the qualities of their veins are that the patient stretches his neck while twisting a little link, as before; then tie it, and make the tie with a short flame, but not too wide, for there is no heat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the fire is subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make an incision for the blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with a cloth, and secure it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The incision of the vein near the nose is effective for ague, scrofula, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of the incision is that the patient holds his neck, then presses his nose to your left hand, takes subtle flame long, and thrusts it into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open easily and the wound will start to heal soon; do not go too deep, make the incision according to necessity, then let it rest for a night, as it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The straining of the second joint aids in the setting of the ankle, and at the beginning of swelling, and many diseases, and infection, and corrosion, and herpes, and abscesses; and the quality of the straining is such that the patient stretches their neck under one and the other, as we have said; and the master standing above the patient, and the patient lies on the seat, then strain the vein gently along its length, then draw the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then close another vein, then untie the ligament, and gently tighten all the veins so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the liver surgery
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The translation of the given line is as follows: "The opening of veins in the lips above helps in cooling in the mouth, and in corruption of the gums, and cuts in the lips, and toothache and around."
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of surgery are to make the patient sit before you and hold his neck as I said; then turn the liver, and look at the two veins, one on the right liver and the other on the left, and they can be recognized by the fact that they are black and have small black veins around them; so seize both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are uncertain, seize the largest of each pair, and also do the same for the veins above and below in the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the liver beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The surgery of the veins beneath the tongue is done after the cephalic surgery, and it is at the incision of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of surgery are that the patient lies down with his hands between the sun, and the tongue is lifted, and look under each side to find a black vein: seize both of them, but do not go too deep, as beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins from which one commonly heals are healed in two ways: either by pricking it with a large instrument made of mirrat or subtle olive oil, and this is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the size and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of mirrtin flames is very renowned, and it is wide as you see: (Translation)
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 It is necessary to open large, plain veins that contain thick and turbulent blood, and this is the form of olive oil fire.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointedly subtle, and is for refining subtle veins with citrus-colored thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The sanctuary of the basilica, one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, neck, chest, and belly; and it is necessary for the healer to bleed profusely and to release the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if the artery is touched and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped as I have said; and the flame should not be pricked but cut like an anvil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilica does not open clearly, you must cut it open and change another one; or you may want to find another route for it, or bleed in its place through the arm vein: it opens clearly; and strike the flame like an anvil, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you want to find the joint of the bone, you must also stretch out the arm, touch the joint until you recognize the pulses; then mark the joint with a cross, bind the arm and burn the vein with the flame carefully; be sure not to cut into the artery when you see the joint swelling, for it is the artery: avoid that.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it rises upwards like a child's urine and the wound is red and tender, know that it is without the artery: hurry then and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding stops, for many times this happens; bind the arm and leave it as it is, let the patient not move it; be afraid and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the wound is not stopped and it bleeds, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, as the head of the artery retracts; stop the bleeding in the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And take a piece of fennel root, cut it and take one half and place it well on the other until the next day; if it does not rot, that's good; if it does, heal it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stopping of bleeding should not be greatly delayed due to the small size of the wound or the thickness of the bandage around the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The vein in the middle helps to treat bleeding from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins as we have said; therefore the healer should cleanse for the nerve that is beneath, and if it bleeds too much, and finds the nerve, inflate and heal it carefully, but may not be able to heal; this nerve opens up often, and if it does not open in some men due to its subtlety, you must treat it with an instrument such as a lancet or a needle; and avoid damaging the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The first aid for the cephalique [head] wound is to draw blood from it and help the eyes; it is necessary to cauterize with olive oil or myrtle fire, as this is the safest of all veins, because there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Furthermore, it is necessary to seek the shallowest vein, and not to worry if it must be done for the first time, and we try again; and sometimes the veins swell in some men, which causes difficulty for the first time, but we should not worry about it.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it should not be done except to preserve health and to prevent future diseases; bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins: cephalique [head], faste [arm] or basilique [leg]; and it should be done at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The cure for the sick is not determined by a fixed hour, but whenever there is need, day or night, at all hours and in every moment; and it is not appropriate to heal children before they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying a child until after the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	They should not heal the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when anyone wishes to be healed, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that their intestines are cleared with a gentle enema if they have retained much gas, so that the veins do not attract waste from the main organs; nor should one heal the one who is too salty from food, or drunk, as long as he continues to be drunk, nor the droplet-prone; and if one wishes to heal after a colic affliction, vomiting, stomach disorder, excessive urination, hard labor, staying awake, exertion, fasting, and those who have recently had sexual intercourse or been wounded, then subtle the humors if they are too heavy, by food and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then immerse [the patient] in water, unless something prevents it, to refine the blood, and heal the vein from the third part, as we have said; and protect that day from labor, pain, lust, and similar things; and be patient and joyful, and let the healer rise higher than the one being healed, and stroke his arm two or three times, then gently pull out the suture above; for when it is too tight or thin, it cannot heal without it; and then stroke the wound with your hands until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the healer's hand with a little old oil, then place his thumb of his left hand below the wound where one wishes to heal, so that the wound does not collapse or fail when striking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 There are veins that flee like cords in a sieve, and some of them are filled with pus, so that when flame is applied, it recoils from the flame and cannot open the vein; such is one's case; and if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, hence the surgeons should be aware of these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that's good; if not, continue a little below or above that spot, unless it is inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 If the thigh is swollen and the patient fears, let him rest for a day or two, and do not bind his arm; perhaps pus-filled abscesses will come out; do not immerse it in water, then resume surgery if he consents; and if the wound is small or narrow, carefully and gently make an incision with a thin knife, and doubt not that there may not be as much blood flowing out as you see; apply the flame directly to the wound and open it slightly so that the thigh swells. Such happens frequently when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the joint swollen, do not start treatment immediately, but put a little bit of oil on it, as oil liquefies the body's blood, and oil is absorbed in this place where the oil is applied; administer the oil in each wound to stop the flow of blood; and similarly, use oil for every artery you treat, to stop the bleeding; and likewise, apply triacle and bowe when placing it on the joint; if it becomes too thick, make it more subtle.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant. Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And there are often abscesses and signs in the sanctuary of the temple: put your hand on it then, if you find it soft to the pressure of your hand, it is an evil sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not place anything of what we have said on it, for by chance in court without the artery; but make one dry compress to harden it, then heal it with another remedy until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for those who are full and swollen, and have a need for the extraction of blood, to make a larger incision, and let the veins be wide; and for the weak ones, do the opposite, and it should be drained little by little, and it should be drained by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of draining is safe from the displacement of blood and the compression of nerves, and it is more effective than long draining rather than wide.

Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if the hand is wounded after much bleeding, then it must be treated with burnt charcoal, a fragrant subtle syrup, and other things as mentioned in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.

If one wants to fracture his arm, and heal it again at another time, if it is weakened by repeated healing, then let him heal little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.

Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 The wound within the body has much blood which is already heated and causes fever; in such cases, a large quantity of blood must be drawn out and the wound opened wide until it stops bleeding. Then you should attend to all the conditions of healing, place your hand over the pulses when it heals, so that death does not occur at the site of bleeding, which happens frequently when healers are negligent; and it is not necessary to dislocate the arm and draw blood again if the wound closes, you should instead press firmly. Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to draw blood a second time, draw it from the same place, or another vein, or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are opened at the location of the neck because they are composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the method of the wound is that the patient puts his hand into hot water, until the flesh becomes red; then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then heal the wound carefully through the cross, not wide or long; and make large wounds, and the wound should be healed close to the joint of the hand, and if one cannot pull it out, put the hand into hot water again, and let the blood come out in the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not strike the hand into hot water again, for it puts more winter there than in summer; and the wound of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The warm salve of the left hand is effective for all liver diseases, and this is how it works: hold the hand, immerse it in hot water until the vein swells if you can see it; if the wound is transverse, cover it completely with everything, it will cause no harm; do not go too deep because the nerves are entirely naked under the skin. Then put the hand back in hot water, but make sure the wound has not frozen and cannot be withdrawn.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as necessary, put oil and wax on the wound to heal quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgative of the hand on the left side is beneficial for the disease of mice, and do as I have told you regarding the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies. And the qualities of his health are that the patient should step into hot water up to his ankle, and rub on top of the vein until it perishes, and tie above the joint of the leg; and the vein is at the knee, and from below the leg there will be much bleeding; thus the wider the blood flow, or at the knee, the better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	If you should raise [the vessel] above the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and pierce it similarly as in cutting; let the flames not burn it.

Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment. Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee of fire, and its lesion is worth the pain of the hinge when it is due to hot blood.

Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't treat it, no remedy for the one who has a joint opened or dislocated near the little finger, and towards the base, keep away from the nerves; do as much compression of the blood as you see fit, then unbind the ligature, put cotton on it and bind it again; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of suction cup remedies
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters are made of horns, or hair, or glass; and blistering is done in two ways: either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 This suction cup treatment is performed in two ways: either it is applied to all parts of the body or not applied to fire; and the suction cup treatment made by wounding and extraction of blood is performed at twelve inches from the heart, so one is entirely on the head, another at the neck, another in the chests of the neck, another under the chin, another at the shoulders, another at the elbows, another at the ankles, another at the feet, another at the wrists, and the suction cup treatment does not treat blood except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it should not be applied in any way to fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from retention, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if it is necessary due to illness that one needs to be bled, or for habitual reasons, we will administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle, and in every time; for there are those who, when they need to be bled, have a heavy head; and there are those who find swelling and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darken the eyes; and there are those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue is swollen, and they drool blood; and there are those who think, and see ghosts and hallucinations and death-like things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially if it is outside of the month, we command to ventose after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The bleeding of the nose helps with headache ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; and this bleeding is instead of the cephalic bloodletting, and those who are cold in constitution or have a fever should not use it, as it does them great harm; and therefore, those with headache illnesses should not use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves often become careless and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the danger of negligence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is located near the jugular vein and basilica, and for this reason it is effective in the restraint of the pis (a disease or condition), and in cutting the channel of the worm, and in piercing, and in filling; and it must be pressed gently, because if it holds too firmly, it may cause obstruction in the bladder or the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosation in the costal part of the neck is effective for headaches, otitis (ear disease), migraines, strangling, and tooth root pain, and it is located near the basilica vein; you must instruct the patient to press gently with their hand, not to hit the artery, and there should be no bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosations below the chin are useful for mouth disease and decay of the gums, as well as similar diseases found in the mouth; it is located near the salivary glands of the two lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations of the shoulders are useful for disease caused by heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres. The blister that is on the buttock is effective against hemorrhoids from their foundation and diseases beneath, and it should be large and made of goose feathers, which requires good drawing; and if it were too fine, it would break; causing large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The blisters on the legs open widely because they draw blood from the entire body, and they are effective against ancient pains of rheumatism, marasmus, and the bladder, and remove inflammation; they are located in the joints of the knees and ankles, and weaken the body after long use, causing paralysis in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the cupping glass is as follows: first make it empty and fill it quickly, then place it immediately, move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the skin turn red and swell, and appear the color of blood; then let it rest, and replace the cupping glasses, and take care in the arrangement of the body, for there are some who have thin skin and clear veins: it is necessary to make a single cut, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and one deep puncture; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If the skin is thick, then it is necessary to make two cuts: the first time to refine the vein's path for thick blood.

Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant. Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amoradine oil, or balm of Gilead oil, or anise oil, and others similar.

Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And guard that the one who is healing is coleric, and if he lacks it excessively and becomes inflamed; then it is necessary that he take cold things, such as watermelons, lettuce and endives; and similar foods; and drink little, eat meat of a rooster, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 If he has a cold complexion, he should take syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is neither old nor new, drink liquorice or musk melon before or after ventilation, to strengthen the main members; let him be thin, but he must not drink if he is hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The following hiccoughs that are placed for wounding are those that are placed on the liver, on the spleen, podagry, on the belly and the buttocks and the flanks and the groin, because these members cannot be wounded elsewhere, and it is done only to draw blood from one member into another, as we do with mammary glands when they are inflamed; for removing viscosity from the member, as we do with ventouses on the belly and the buttocks for reducing swelling; and for alleviating pain, where there is an abscess or a stone, it draws the abscess by chance using its attractive power or removes the stone from its place; and in this way, it functions when placed on the liver and the spleen where there is retained wind, and these ventouses are administered empty for squeezing only; sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, such as in cases of pleurisy, and in this manner, a ventouse is filled with hot saline solution or with hot water in which herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the bladder administered to fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers and half a palm wide, and have a small hole pierced through the middle, as for pushing an awl, and made of bone, soft in front so as not to prick the patient when placing it on the member; and in the middle there should be a rod of bone or iron, for setting a splint, and they should be large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who suffer from them; for the boils of children are different than those of the elderly, and thin ones than thick.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this splint should be placed on the member in the following manner: take the linen or wax and place it inside the hole in the splint, so that the light is at the bottom of the splint to prevent burning the patient; then place it on the member, with the fingers over the hole as we have said before, so that when one looks, if steam escapes, the splint is removed; and linen or wax is taken again as before, and repeated frequently, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder, which is administered in disease of pleurisy, not sharp nor pointed, and is not administered unless it is full of liquid, and is placed only on the member; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Bladders are not administered in small members, such as lips and gums, or similar places; and in naked skin areas, such as fingers or nails, and other similar areas; and the quality of the user is that when you find bladders which are in clear, clean sweet urine, take them; put them in a container with clean sweet urine until they become familiar and have nothing inside them; then they should be drained through vein and bladder, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the bladders on it; when they are full and warm, if it is in a place where a bladder can be placed, place it there, for it works very well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If the shoulder is not dislocated, raise the arm gently and then immerse it in cold water, afterwards rub it; and if the arm remains diseased too long within the body, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it, until the sores are dried; and if the sores multiply, place crushed vitriol or gall, and similar things, until they are dried; or place half of raw beans on the shoulder and leave them until they adhere to the shoulder, which will now stop the bleeding; and if you have more need, take other arteries.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the arteries do not want to drain, rub the arm with fresh blood, or you insert a needle until the blood comes out, and then place them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will clot; and when you see that they bleed, sprinkle a little of aloe and frankincense powder, or ash, which will now stop the bleeding.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that the foolish man despises this chapter, for he never sees any of the old books or reads their letters; and because of this, the science is foreign to our land, for I have never found anyone good at it; and I do not know anything about it, except by the knowledge of the old books which I have studied so much that I have treated the subject and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments brought forth, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to say the prologue of this book the summary of speech and chapters where wise men put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who have experience know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 When a fracture or dislocation or torsion or curvature comes to someone, it is necessary that you quickly clean the patient from one side and the other, unless something stops you, such as weakness of the body, or infants, or elderly; or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and avoid cold meat, namely cold cuts and meat eye and shin, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fat meats, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about the abscess being hot or of the spreading of matter to the member; if the patient returns to his first proper government as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that make thick broths, or they have thickness, such as cooked wheat in water, and meat of the head, and feet, and pancreas of cow, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	In prolonged nursing, the wounds break more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that the broken bones of the elderly and weak cannot be well regained or joined according to their nature due to the relaxation of the limbs, neither those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but pay no heed, set above the broken bone large splints which hold and join the limb together, until it hardens as it was before; and do not let him move it at all, and for this reason feed him with large foods, as we have said.
