Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture occurs in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, make it straight as required; bind it with the palm, and if you see that it needs a splint to lift the fracture and not move; and if the fracture is in other fingers such as the index or others, make them straight, and bind them with the adjacent healthy finger. Or tie all of them together in one place, for moving is harmful, or put a splint on it, as with a thumb; take care in the restoration and the setting of the abscess and be careful to treat those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The leg bones are often broken, and one sees it when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one places one splint above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each assistant extends their splint to their equal portion; and this is when the break has been set in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is close to the root of the hip, it may be one of the ligaments towards the knee, and the other ligaments on the opposite side of the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is close to the knee, then the ligaments should be on the side of the knee, and the extension below; then align the bone with both hands according to its natural shape, and then apply a splint, and bandage, as long as no abscess comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, let it cool first, then return to your work and treatment; the remedy is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 You must wrap above the fracture and bind it tightly in two or three layers, and remove the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and pass a long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and bring the ends of the thread above; then turn the leg and the bandage above the leg and above the hip, then place splints on the fracture and a splint on the bone of the leg; then use soft cloth for seven inches between the leg and the thigh to straighten the splint, then start tying three or four turns above the fracture; and as you move further from the fracture, you should loosen the splint; then take hold of the two threads you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return to below the thread ends, so that you reach the foot; tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it as it is, until no abscess or swelling or any other similar thing comes out.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, unbind and correct what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are bone pieces that protrude, they must be cut, if possible; and if not, the place must be broken and drained, and treated as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone is broken in such a way that splints are placed there, as in the shoulder or arm; however, in the healing process, this does not cause discomfort to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is healed within a few days or a little more or less, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee joint occurs little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not really a fracture, but rather a split or piercing, causing pain at every wound and this hurts greatly.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one equalizes the limb that is dislocated with its opposite, as long as it can be assembled in movement; then put the splint, and place a round peg if necessary, and tighten it as needed, then reposition all the alignments that we have said in other breaks, such as abscesses and others; place at each accident what is required, as long as it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called the "ham", and the other is called the "shin"; and it breaks in the same way as the arm does, and therefore its treatment is the same as that of the arm, and the work is equal. And if both bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the slender bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 If the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; and it turns underneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply extension, and make it even, and tie the limbs equally; however, if the break is ugly and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; align accordingly to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two pieces of splints that span the leg on both sides and are as long as from the knee to below; then wrap them in two layers, one above and one below, and tie them in the middle as well, so that the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should apply a splint of wood along the length of the leg, but rather a bandage, and place the leg for preventing movement, and carefully make this at the break where there is pain; and move the leg every day, to see if there is an abscess or other accident; treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break, but sometimes breaks occur in the bones of the foot and toes, and it requires certain treatment in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see the bones rising against each other, put the patient lying on his back with his foot raised, as if he were walking, then place your hand under where the bones are raised, press them back to their places; then cover it with plaster and wool and place a small table with two even surfaces beneath the belly of the foot, then tie the foot in place with bandages and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandages, for you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said for the bones in the hand; then place a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and let it be slightly larger, then place under the bone that table I mentioned, and hold it securely; and if there are 2 or more, or more, break each bone and place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the bone under the skin; and let the table be positioned above the belly of the bone, so that it touches well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And do not forget the other things I have said about broken bones, after we have discussed them; and treat each case according to its circumstances.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of the female nature is broken, make her sit with her back leaning, and hold it from behind; then fill the wound of the patient with cloth and also as large as necessary; then turn the woman, lift the buttocks little by little, and then push the cloth until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and the bone comes out with the stick; when she wants to urinate, remove the cloth, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or so: the break will be healed, and if you see, take a bladder of barley, and tie one end to the wound, and blow all the bladder into the wound; then forcefully exhale through the tube until the bladder is inflated inside: the bone will return to its place; then fill with cloth, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the arm is broken for either man or woman, restore it in the manner as we have said in the thigh-bone; and these nearby breaks shall not be concealed from him who applies his study and skill, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 The break signifies in various ways the correct course of restoration: so then do it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In a staff when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and put the staff in it; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	for the one who has a breakage with wound, particularly if it is large, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or something similar, that it should be treated now, so that the sores mentioned previously bear witness to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, apply vinegar to it, if you have none else, then begin again to heal the breakage in that same hour, or on that day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes up, wait until the ninth day for it to be soothed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad incident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears exposed on the edge of the wound, you must set it gently in place with light pressure and extend it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not appear equal for you to set in place, then use this instrument that is made of iron, which is 7 or 8 inches long and the width is according to the size of the wound; therefore, the mirror must grasp 3 or 4 fingers, depending on what is needed for each bone-setting treatment; and it should be round and somewhat large but not too thin so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and it should be sharp in front and thick from the middle forward, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "thigh-bone", for this reason the curved heads should be placed on top of the visible part of the bone; and push it once until it returns, and they should be even with one another.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 If the break is subtle and the instrument cannot properly take hold of the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, within your power; then remove what remains sharp and in small fragments from the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is set, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Then put it in its place, then moisten the linen with black stiptic wine, and apply it properly if it is hot; do not put any oil or ointment on the wound that might cause pus and corruption; then administer some bandages when you have set the bone, leave the wound open, cover it with a dressing according to the size of the wound, and be careful not to strain the wound with the fracture; many times the foolish surgeon has caused this to happen, causing harm or even death to the patient; and the bindings should be softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come, as we have said, and you feel pain at its place, do not put on splints; but wrap around it instead, in place of splints, hard bandages and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one or two days swelling at the wound, remove whatever you have put on it entirely and apply healing ointment for wounds such as tetrafarmacons and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, once in the morning and once in the evening, as long as it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be aligned in such a manner that the bone moves down gently but gradually.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes many days and cannot heal but the bone keeps moving, since there are small pieces of bone, which is why you should press the wound with pressure, and remove all those dislocated pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula or any kind of corruption comes at the place, you must treat it, according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and open at the limb, such as the femur or shoulder bones, and other similar large members, do not draw it out because many times death comes from it; but leave it until it can set itself; perhaps it will heal itself after 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The coming sores on the sore (translated as: 'the sores that come upon a sore')
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There are often times after the fracturing of health that it occurs again, especially near the joint, and it is a displeasing sight to see the figure of the limb; and by chance the limbs cannot perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the limb is fresh: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocola, acacia, and similar ones, so that you take any of these things or all together, and crush them with a sharp liquid such as vinegar or egg white or oil; then apply it to the knot in poultices, and keep it tightly wrapped and not loosen it for many days; and then dislocate it, and begin another, until the swelling subsides; or you may hold it on a piece of wood well-made because the properties of wood are such that they remove all inflammations from the limbs; and if the nodule has already become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut the top off, and reveal the superfluous part; or you may shave it with a razor, until it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb which is weak after being set (or treated)
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains weak and tender after that, it happens for many reasons: one is when it was bound too tightly and was not bound as it should have been; or when there were too many splints, and the nutrients could not reach the member; or due to excessive rubbing; or due to excessive movements, not at the appropriate time; or because there is little blood in the body, so it remains weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body become strong, until the blood multiplies within him; then administer baths, and give joy and pleasure; afterwards put ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts great nutrients to it, and rub it frequently with cold water, until the nutrients reach the member; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The member twisted out of health [or order] after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is disfigured, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great harm comes from it, and sometimes death; however, if the dislocation and torture are fresh, then they must be treated with hot water or softening herbs such as vismalve leaves, roots, medick, and similar things; and you should make a soothing poultice, such as dittany well made, and take musk from vismalve, mix it with beeswax or camphor oil, and apply the poultice; or you may use figs softened with wheat bran, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is opened by rubbing continually and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is grown and hardened, as stone, and needs to be cut with iron, it should be covered up to the bone, at the incision made subtly and gently; and put on a cushion and bandage in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it must now be reset without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if you delay, the joint swells, and in case it is reset on small bones; therefore, it should not be moved when it is swollen: many times it brings spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then let him rest, until the abscesses calm down; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently move it, and cure each limb as it will come in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jawbones are dislocated on both sides, and dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are slightly dislodged from their places and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the cheek, and saliva drools out of the mouth that it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and it wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a small dislocation returns with various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is whole and complete, you must quickly reset it, without delaying; and in such a way that the servant holds the head of the patient, and pushes one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is from two parts; and the other hand should be pulled aside, to make them equal; and command the patient to soften their jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror set even again, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jawbones are dislocated, anoint them with hot water and oil, gently adjusting them until they are set; do not force it to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are reset equally, and the mouth of the patient closes well, put on it a cushion filled with soft material made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with several bands; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his arms between two pillows so that it does not move to either side or makes an effort to move, but takes light food until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not strain himself in opening the mouth to eat and drink, until the jaws are well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be properly set within an hour and are not returned to their places, then fever and accustomed sweats occur, and possibly rupture of the stomach, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is lost causes; and many times the person who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	Of the collarbone
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The collarbone cannot dislocate towards the chest and ribs from the inside, nor can it dislocate outwards; however, it sometimes does dislocate, which is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and stretches out his arms; then presses the joint firmly with your hand, and it will return; then put a splint and bandage on it, and hold it in place; and the dislocated shoulder cannot dislocate again; if it does, reset it to its place as we have said; then put a splint and bandage on it, and hold it in place, and tell the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus the shoulders of the back are also reset when they are dislocated.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The dislocation of the shoulder   (from the previous sentence)
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways: the first is when it dislocates at the socket below; and the second is at the hip part; and occasionally it dislocates above the part, but this rarely happens; it does not dislocate behind the shoulder nor inside the nerves; and often it dislocates below towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, because it can be easily forced out; in those who have enough flesh, it is forced out only slightly, and returns only slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men percussion or breaking, and swells the shoulder with an abscess hot, and believes that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must check it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocation occurs downwards towards the socket, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest difference; and at the top of the shoulder, you will find a hollow, and beneath the socket, where the top of the shoulder touches the socket, as if it were an eye; and the sick cannot bring their hand back to its place, nor can they make any movement; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly at the socket; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to return, except when the infant is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand up high, then places his fists under the joint, and forcibly moves the joint upward to its place; and the minister lifts the hand, extends it upwards, puts it back in place; it will come back immediately.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if the dislocation does not come as we have said in many days afterwards, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and bring soothing, softening and calming remedy, such as a concoction of elderflower, fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and administer it; then lay the patient on his back, and place a piece of equal linen fabric under the affected shoulder, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the heel of the other assistant on the fabric, and lift the head of the shoulder skillfully, and pull the arm of the patient; another assistant holds the head of the patient to prevent him from moving forward; the affected shoulder returns immediately, and if you see it dislocate again in this manner: then make a person larger than the patient be present; he should be facing towards the side, and push the affected shoulder under the patient's affected shoulder, lift the patient's affected shoulder upwards so that the patient hangs on the arm, and another assistant pulls the patient's arm downward toward his stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too weak, he cannot lift anything heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And it is also done in another way: and it is as one pushes the long needle into the ground, so that the head should be aligned like the pistil, and not too thick nor too thin; then it is placed beneath the patient but with a cloth soft on top, and the patient remains lying down; then his hand is extended from the other side to form a hook, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, this treatment is done: take the needle of two hands wide and four fingers long, which has its head rounded for entering deeply beneath the ascle, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the rod on top of the patient's head, so that the rod does not pierce the patient, then put it underneath the sick person's shoulder; extend one arm above the rod, and place the shoulder above the rod, and the arm to the top of the hand, then put the arm on a 1-inch block from a scale, and let the hands hang down below; the joint will be reduced now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever way that may be, you must place an equal sphere of wool underneath the shoulder, then apply the plaster made of milled powder, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then hold it underneath the shoulder carefully, and twist the linen around the plaster, and bind the hands to their neck, and let them remain in that position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is necessary that he eats little food, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then eat less after 5 or 7 days, and move it; if it becomes hardened and does not soften, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture which has come or for some other reason, then you must apply fire cauterization at three points, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the jointure does not hold, and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder has been cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the jointure should never be forced back into its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	A dislocation that is towards the buttocks or backside, and the limbs, should be treated by pushing and stretching with hands, and other means; and it should be cured until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing comes swelling in the member and it gradually moves, then the patient should use baths many times until the swelling subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	The cost of dislocation is...
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	When the joint is dislocated at the point, it will come back to the same place again; and if dislocated in all parts, front and back, and the dislocation is not repaired because it can be seen and felt clearly; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick body with healthy one, make sure to see them clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is stiff, and cannot bend the arm nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it when abscesses have grown there, for if abscesses have grown there, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset in all places, especially when it is at the back; it is more difficult than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes there.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	Then the restoration is such that you extend your two hands towards it; his arms should be spread out, and the hands turned as much as possible around it, inside and outside, and push the joint back to its pockets, or to the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and bend the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 If it does not return to its place, apply strong extension; and there are two persons extending the arm, and two persons pressing it so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm on each side, when you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide around it; and when the healer joins the joint with his hand, oil it to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg, and hold it firmly, and bind the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then unbind.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the jointure is fixed in its place, break the ligament, and leave it; and if you see that the jointure does not hold well, repeat the manipulation and the ligament, and leave it like that for some days, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if there is pain after the resetting of the joint, and it swells, wash and rub it gently, and press until it is soothed; or you place a sheep's fat pad on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and have it enter the bath; and when it sweats, wipe the joint gently, then place the fat pad back, and then enter it in the bath; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, place warm moist hay wrapped in butter on it, and apply pressure; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand's joint is easy to relocate compared to other jointures, it must be returned to its place quickly, during the very moment when it is dislocated, unless the lews are inflamed or there is an abscess heat.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting of the hand, you place the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and align the fingers, so that the palm is placed above the appearance of the joint, and push until it returns to its normal position; it is necessary that you observe whether it is in the correct place; then have the patient lie down his hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on the table, and have them put their other hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it is well; if not, apply a pressure plaster to the abscess, and leave it in place for it to heal.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot tolerate it and you cannot put it back after any days, the dislocated joint remains so; this does not harm the patient as long as his hand is disabled and he cannot strain anything at all: therefore know that the nerves are severed or the arteries; there is no other remedy except to apply a fire cautery in this case, and perhaps nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at its place, put on the plaster as we have said, then strain it and leave for 5 days, then release and let it rest.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move properly and there is no swelling, wet with warm water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 When the fingers of the hand are dislocated on both sides, or at the back of the palm or the belly; then you hold the dislocation in place with your thumbs until it returns, then you hold the head of the finger and turn it towards the side where it is disjoined; and leave it for two days, and then make it straight that day; and tie it as we have said, and untie it the next day, and make it move, and reattach it; and do this often, until it becomes narrow, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	And also for the dislocation of the vertebra in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra in the back or neck is dislocated, and if there are multiple dislocations without any treatment, death quickly comes to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that the excretions jump without will, and cannot be held; they are often softened in any member, either the two legs or the two arms or the backbone; when the backbone becomes silent at four parts; that which becomes silent in the back is called "gilbositez": the remedy is to check if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if it has not been cured or healed since then.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of cure say in great words, but there is not much benefit in all this; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the hernia that comes before, there is no remedy nor health; and similarly the one that comes directly to both sides, and can only be cured by the one coming from behind, as I have said; and it is that the patient should be spread out on his face in one place, and have a support underneath him, so he does not bleed; then stick the needle into the head in the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a cord over the hernia of the patient, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two assistants know the cords, one at the head and others at the feet, between the two needles; and they should be well closed, the needles as we have said, and the assistant places his palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if the dislocation does not return by this cure, then take a table three spans long and shaped like a wedge, and position the patient on their side. Push the head of the table under the opening, then place the handle of the table on the spine. Place your hands on either end of the table and press firmly until it returns to its place. If you see it, do so on the turntable that turns with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And take two needles of a great span in length and place them on either side of the patient's head, with a palm's length of space between each needle. Place a small stone or weight at the end of each needle to keep it in place, ensuring that they do not move. Between the two needles, insert a third needle that can rotate like ropes, with two small needles of a palm's length on either side of it for turning the rotating needle. Then tie the cords that pass through the openings to the rotating needle at the head and the other cords to the rotating needle at the feet, allowing each assistant to turn their respective rotating needle fully. The master will ensure the spine remains in its proper alignment as described earlier.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is aligned, put on it a plaster with desiccant made from egg and then bandage it, and afterwards place an elm stick of three feet long, pushing it through the thickened part and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a rope as we have said, and make the patient use gentle rocking until it is healed; and if something comes at the end of the healing process, administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the stick mentioned earlier; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes the appearance is in the back spondyle of the spine, and it seems to be dislocation; but this is the bone that opens, which should not be presumed: maybe death will come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of the dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The dislocations of the shoulder and those of the elbow joint come from nowhere but only dislocations; and the shoulder joint is dislocated in four ways: internally and externally, front and back, more internally than otherwise, slightly dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when the sick leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and wider open at the knee than the healthy, and the sick person cannot bend their knee in fire; and it is the joint which is displaced due to abscess heat that is swollen, because the thigh of the calf comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes to discharge (or expel), is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one whose leg is well-set according to the completion; however, do not double the knee due to pain, and if you want it to walk, it cannot move forward, and it retains its urine, and when it walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one whose condition is behind (or posterior), are that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and the leg is twisted more than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this kind of dislocation are that you watch if the dislocations are old and remain in place according to their position, without any treatment; and it is not necessary that there be any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	For the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of four kinds of dislocation, hasten that you turn the joint, and push it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, it will not need any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this way, then you must call for a strong servant and hold the leg firmly with both hands or tied above the knee; another servant extends his hand in such a manner that he puts his hands under the shin, then tightens a rope ligament above the calf; another holds the thigh of the ligament; and extend upwards and downwards all at once so that the patient is lifted off the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This way of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If not, it is necessary to treat the condition when the dislocation is at the front. It is necessary that you place the patient on their healthy side, then tie a rope around the root of the hip, and the part that is under the angle, then pull the rope up towards the angle and towards the forceps; then take another attendant and grasp the large hip of the affected limb and extend it outward in the opposite direction; it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot set it in this manner as we have said, it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient tightly with a strong rope around both ankles and both knees, and the affected leg should be extended two fingers' breadth more than the other; then hang him by his head on a pole, and let his arms hang down for two spans from the ground; then command the attendant to seize the hip of the affected limb, and let another attendant hold on with the patient, who will grasp the limb in turn, because the joints return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocations are displaced, if the patient lies down, as we have said in those with gout, and stretches the ligament above the diseased leg and similarly on the arm; then put the splints, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert the splint between the knees of the patient in the proper form; and plant damp cloths around it so that it does not burn the patient, then extend each minister toward him, and place the mirror equally against his hand for the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it comes back, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If it does not come back, place him on a table and press as we have said in the case of gout, and make the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must be extended as quickly as possible, according to what I said earlier; and place the mirror on the opposite side of the diseased limb, then press with the other hand, and turn it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is to the outside, it should not extend the patient below, nor raise him up off the ground, but rather he should be as if the shoulder was dislocated to the outside, as we have said in the lying down on two beds; and it should be on its face, and the limbs extended as we have said before, and it should press on the joint to the table; and when the patient extends his legs and they are even, then align the thighs, and place the pillow, and bind with a bandage so that the shoulder does not move; and rest for three or four days, then unbind, and place the pillow again; and if you see that they are even, bind as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind, and let him walk gently until the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee dislocates in three ways: inside and out, behind, and not in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit straight, extend his leg if he can, place your back on his thigh, and place his foot on your feet; then take his kneecap in your hands, pull it between your palms, then bend both sides of the kneecap outwards; another assistant extends his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that it should be properly bent at the knee lightly; apply the plaster and hold the leg to the thigh firmly for three or four days, then release it; do not allow the patient to walk until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not present, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it tries to move forward towards the part where it is dislocated: the readjustment is easy, and it should be gently extended with the hands when only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is fully dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left hand twice, then lift it up, and push the foot hard upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, start again, for it will return; and if it cannot return, lay the patient on his back on the ground, and fix the splint firmly in the ground between his thighs, and wrap cloth around it so as not to hurt the patient; then hold the leg straight by the minister, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is set (the dislocation), place the plaster and poultice on top, and hold it in place, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle so the ligaments are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligaments weaken, reset it; then release it on the third day or fourth, and make the patient walk for four days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess swells up, you must treat it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy.
des dois	The two [things] (or parts)
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two [things] are dislocated, they must be stretched gently without strain, and it is an easy task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any notch of the back or foot joints, then you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a chair straight, and place your foot above the openings of these jointures, press your foot firmly until it comes back; and when it is even, and there is no opening, place a two-toed table under the foot's sole, then hold it in place, leave it for three days, then release; let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and it is to be restored, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment, if you are not skilled in the art or have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, yet not hasty; and use, at first, cooling agents on the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of healing; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, as soon as the abscess subsides; and when the limb is in place, administer cooling agents on the abscess again, and heal the wound, as necessary, with dry ointments; and if there is a break along with dislocation, and small bones are displaced, set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear, as I have said, because it will affect you according to your Creator, and for the sake of your knowledge and body's health.
Amen	 Amen (In English)
